310	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">ARMS ACT, 1878 AND ARMS RULES, 1924</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Citation:</b>  40 DLR (AD) 170,40 DLR 251, 40 (AD) 170,44 DLR 110,41 DLR 524, 4I DLR 524, 40 DLR 493,44 DLR 159,43 DLR 150</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  1878</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  ARMS</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2018-01-08</p><!DOCTYPE html><div style="box-sizing: border-box; color: #333333; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; text-align: center;"><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;"><u style="box-sizing: border-box;">Arms Act, 1878</u></span></div><div style="box-sizing: border-box; color: #333333; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; text-align: justify;"> <br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;">Sections 16 &amp; 18—</span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/>Appellant was neither given any notice of enquiry nor was he given any hearing before cancellation of arms—Enquiry undertaken on a sprawling private complaint made by the local upazila Chairman.<br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/>No emergency or any other compelling situation  preventing  giving of notice of enquiry lo the appellant—Nothing on record to show that any specific case was started against the appellant involving alleged misuse of revolver —Inquisitorial nature of enquiry aggravating the degree of unfairness—Principles of natural justice to be observed in proceedings affecting "the person or property or other right of parties concerned "—court adds a rider to the observance of the principle of natural justice that so far as exercise of power under section 18 of the Arms Act is concerned, the absence of a prior notice or hearing may not always invalidate the order passed thereunder if the security of the public peace is involved.<br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;"><em style="box-sizing: border-box;">Sk. Ali Ahmed Vs. Secretary, Home Affairs 40 DLR (AD) 170.</em></span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/> <br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;">Sections 16(1) and 19(1)—</span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/>The  Sub-Divisional Magistrate, Shariatpur had no jurisdiction whatsoever to cancel the license s of the guns in question under section 18(a) of the Arms Act or under any provision of the Arms Rules of 1924. As the license s of the guns in question were not cancelled by any legally competent authority such as the District Magistrate or by any authorised officer to whom he is subordinate as required under the provisions of Arms Act or the Arms rules, cancellation thereof by the SDO is illegal. Conviction under sections 16(1) and 19(1) of the Arms Act read with section 26 of the Special Powers Act is not sustainable in law.<br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;"><em style="box-sizing: border-box;">Anawar  Hossains. Vs State  40 DLR </em></span><em style="font-weight: bold; box-sizing: border-box;">251.</em></div><div style="box-sizing: border-box; color: #333333; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; text-align: justify;"> <br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;">Section 18—</span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/>Cancellation and suspension of license for arms—The necessity of recording reasons by the appropriate authority in writing for the cancellation of the license to be emphasized as a general rule—If the appropriate authority chooses not to make its order a speaking one and merely relies on the materials on record, its order stands a greater risk of being struck down. <br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;"><em style="box-sizing: border-box;">Sk. Ali Ahmed Vs. Secretary Home Affairs 40 (AD) 170.</em></span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/> <br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;">Section 18—</span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/>Orders passed by the District Magistrate cancelling license s of guns of the petitioners without giving them any notice and opportunity of being heard and giving no reason for cancellation are illegal being violative of the principal of natural justice.<br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;"><em style="box-sizing: border-box;">Rezaul Karim (Md) Vs. Ministry of Home Affairs 44 DLR 110.</em></span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/> <br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;">Section 19A—</span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/>Uncorroborated testimony of an accomplice cannot be basis of conviction of an accused.<br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;"><em style="box-sizing: border-box;">Kazi ibrahim Vs State 41 DLR 524.</em></span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/> <br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;">Section 19A—</span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/>A person cannot be convicted on surmises and conjectures and from any analogical deduction.<br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;"><em style="box-sizing: border-box;">Kazi Ibrahim VS. State 4I DLR 524.</em></span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/> <br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;">Section 19(f)—</span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/>Appellants leading the police to place of occurrence and recovery of arms—Appellants cannot be held guilty of the charge of unauthorised possession of arms under section 19(f) of the Arms Act.<br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;"><em style="box-sizing: border-box;">Abdul Khaleque Vs. State 40 DLR 493.</em></span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/> <br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;">Section 19(f)—</span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/>Recovery of arms—culpability—mere knowledge of the accused that the arms were lying at the spot pointed out by him in the absence of evidence that he himself kept the same there or that he had exclusive possession over it, he cannot be made liable under section 19(f).<br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;"><em style="box-sizing: border-box;">Abul Hashem Master Vs. State 44 DLR 159.</em></span><br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/> </div><div style="box-sizing: border-box; color: #333333; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; text-align: center;"><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;"><u style="box-sizing: border-box;">Arms Rules, 1924</u></span></div><div style="box-sizing: border-box; color: #333333; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; text-align: justify;"> <br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/>Column 2 of the Table Schedule I as amended by notification No 896—Section II dated Dhaka the l9th November l973—The decision in this case having depended on findings of facts as to whether the seized arm were recovered from the possession of the petitioner, whether the same came within the exception provided for and covered by amnesty, if any, declared by the government, the extraordinary power to prevent the abuse of process of the court is not required to be exercised.<br style="box-sizing: border-box;"/><span style="box-sizing: border-box; font-weight: bold;"><em style="box-sizing: border-box;">Hossain Mohammad Ershad Vs. State 43 DLR 150</em></span></div></div></div>
311	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Money Laundering Portirodh Ain, 2002</h2>

5.4pt;	mso-para-margin-top:0in;	mso-para-margin-right:0in;	mso-para-margin-bottom:10.0pt;	mso-para-margin-left:0in;	line-height:115%;	mso-pagination:widow-orphan;	font-size:11.0pt;	mso-bidi-font-size:14.0pt;	font-family:"Calibri","sans-serif";	mso-ascii-font-family:Calibri;	mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;	mso-hansi-font-family:Calibri;	mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;}</style><![endif]--></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 11.05pt 0in 0.0001pt 15.1pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">                               Money Laundering Portirodh Ain, 2002</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.15in; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 13</span></strong></p><p class="Style6" style="text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Appellate Division observed that the High Court Division made the observation and direction that on perusal of the First Information Report and the charge sheet, it appears that the alleged money was transferred from the joint account of Mr. Julfikar Ali and his wife Rahima Ali to the account of the present accused petitioner and her husband, accused Md. Hafiz Ibrahim in Singapore for illegal purchase but said Mr. Julfikar Ali and his wife were not made accused in the case, though Julfiker Ali has been cited as a witness in the charge <a href="http://sheet.lt"><span style="color: navy;">sheet.lt</span></a> is surprising to High Court that why said Julfikar Ali and his wife were not made accused in the case. From the materials on record, prima facie it seems to High Court that they also committed offence of money laundering as defined in section 2(W) (A) (B) of the Money Laundering Portirodh Ain,2002. The High Court inclined to direct the Anti-Corruption Commission to look into the matter and to take appropriate steps in accordance with the law. The Anti-Corruption Commission did not follow the judgment of the High Court Division. The Assistant Director, Anti-Corruption Commission issued<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>a<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>memo<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>dated 11.09.2014.</span></p><p class="Style6" style="text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">According to that memo if Julfikar Ali had been made an accused, there would be no witness to produce and prove any document in Court. Since there was no other option, Julfikar Ali was made a witness. The aforesaid views expressed in the memo are objectionable and derogatory to the observation and direction made by the High Court Division. It is not comprehensible of how the Anti-Corruption Commission took such a stand in respect of Julfikar Ali. Having considered all aspects of the case, the Appellate Division direct the Special Judge to treat Julfikar Ali and his wife Rahima Ali as accused in the case and to take cognizance against them under the relevant provisions of law and thereafter to proceed with the case in accordance </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">with law<strong> . </strong><em>Mafruza Sultana -Vs.- The State 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)86</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 8.15pt 0in 0.0001pt 26.9pt; text-indent: 4.8pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">         </span>Mitigating circumstances in commuting sentence of death.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.05pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The facts that the condemned petitioner has no previous criminal record, the youth of the petitioner at the time of commission of the offence and he being in the condemned cell for more than 7 years during which period the sword of death was hanging over his lead, have been adjudged as mitigating circumstances warranting commutation of the sentence of death to one of imprisonment for life. <em>Nalu -Vs- The State 1 ALR (AD)222</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.5pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Medical evidence:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Dr. Rathinadra Nath Majumder (PW 14) found Blackish skin of the upper part of the anterior chest wall, 12"x8". Blackish skin of the anterior surface and bath lateral surface of the neck 5" X neck breath. Swollen of the neck and upper part of the anterior chest wall 12" x8". Dr. PW 14, on dissection Antemortem clotted blood found under the skin of the upper anterior chest wall and under the skin of the neck (anterior and bath lateral surface). There is congestion of trachea and esophagus and neck muscles of the above mentioned area. Patecheal hemorrhage of the both lungs. He recorded opinion that the victim died due to asphyxia as a result of strangulation which is atemortem and homicidal in nature. <em>The State -Vs.- Belial Hossain 5 ALR (HCD)2015 (1) 285</em></span></p></div></div>

table.MsoNormalTable	{mso-style-name:"Table 5.4pt;	mso-para-margin-top:0in;	mso-para-margin-right:0in;	mso-para-margin-bottom:10.0pt;	mso-para-margin-left:0in;	line-height:115%;	mso-pagination:widow-orphan;	font-size:11.0pt;	mso-bidi-font-size:14.0pt;	font-family:"Calibri","sans-serif";	mso-ascii-font-family:Calibri;	mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;	mso-hansi-font-family:Calibri;	mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;}</style><![endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-fareast-theme-font: minor-fareast; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-language: BN;">Any man who contracts another marriage meaning that it is the man who contracts the 2nd marriage without permission of the Arbitration Council shall be liable for punishment for such offence but under this section the abettor cannot be proceeded with. Since the said Ordinance has not made any provision providing punishment for abetment of the said offence, the abettor, who-ever he may be, can not be proceeded against for alleged abetment of offence punishable under section 6 (5) of the said Ordinance. <em>Abdulla Mamoon (Rabin). - Vs. - Md. Mahtab Uddin. 3 ALR(2014)(1) 366.</em></span></p><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 6(5) and 7 - Remanding the case to enable the complainant /respondent to adduce and examine more witnesses.</span></strong></p><p class="Style6" style="text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The High Court Division is swayed to the finding that the learned Appellate Court below was absolutely right to hold that there was no divorce between the accused and the complaint's as provisions in section 7 of the Muslim Family Law Ordinance 1961, was not complied with. The High Court Division also note with approval the learned Appellate Court below's finding that the complainant was deprived of the opportunity to adduce enough witnesses to prove her claim, particularly by adducing witness and papers to settle the issue as to whether or not Arbitration Council's permission was obtained. The High Court Division is of view, in the attendant circumstances, the Appeal Court below entertained no error by remanding the case to enable the complainant /respondent to adduce and examine more witnesses.</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="Style6" style="text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Md. Del war Hossain - Vs.- The State <span style="letter-spacing: 1.0pt;">6</span> <span style="letter-spacing: 1.0pt;">ALR-</span> 2015(2)148</span></em></p><p> </p></div></div>
313	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Administrative Tribunal Act 1981</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Citation:</b>  6 BLC (AD) 94, 7 BLC 44, 9 BLC 342, 7 BLC 120, 10 BLC (AD) 193, 8 BLC (AD) 80</p><p><b>Case Year:</b> .0001pt; text-align: center; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 14pt; color: black;">Administrative Tribunal Act 1981</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: normal;"><span style="font-size: 14pt; font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif; color: black;">[VII of 1981]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: normal;"><span style="font-size: 14pt; font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif; color: black;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><span style="color: black;">Section </span></strong><strong><span style="color: black;">4</span></strong><strong><span style="color: black;">—</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><span style="color: black;"> </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif; color: black;">Considering the legal position the Administrative<sub>:</sub>Tribunal found that the case was filed well within time. The Administrative Appellate Tribunal also came to the finding that the respondent had option to move the Director-General under Rule 1725 of the Railway Establishment Code which has been accordingly done and the case has been filed within six months from the order passed by the Director-General. No illegality and wrong has been committed by the Tribunals below. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif; color: black;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><em><span style="color: black;">Director-General/ Secretary, Railway Division and others vs Md Elahi Baksha 6 BLC (AD) 94.</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><span style="color: black;">Section </span></strong><strong><span style="color: black;">4</span></strong><strong><span style="color: black;">—</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><span style="color: black;"> </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><span style="color: black;">If the eligible person is not considered for promotion, in such case the </span><span style="color: black;">aggrieved person can enforce his right by invoking constitutional jurisdiction of the High Court Division as such right cannot be enforced by invoking the jurisdiction of the Administrative Tribunal. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif; color: black;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><em><span style="color: black;">M'Abu Raihan vs Secretary, Ministry of Science and Technology, Bangladesh Secretariat and others 7 BLC </span></em><span style="color: black;">44.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><span style="color: black;">Section </span></strong><strong><span style="color: black;">4</span></strong><strong><span style="color: black;">— </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><span style="color: black;"> </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif; color: black;">Administrative Tribunal is the proper forum as it is the proper fact finding body to go into facts as alleged by the petitioners and grant necessary relief if they were so entitled as the petitioners have not challenged the vires of the law on the basis of which Roads and Railway Division has been created and the posts of the former Railway Division have been abolished by the respondents. Except the assertion by the learned Advocate of malafide action there is no facts averred in all the five writ petitions constituting malafide action leading to passing of the impugned orders. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif; color: black;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><em><span style="color: black;">Karimun Nessa and others vs Government of Bangladesh and others 9 BLC </span></em><span style="color: black;">342.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><span style="color: black;">Section </span></strong><strong><span style="color: black;">4(2)</span></strong><strong><span style="color: black;">—</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><span style="color: black;"> </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif; color: black;">Even if the gradation list has the force of law concerning the terms and conditions of the service of the petitioners it would not enable the petitioners to seek remedy under the writ jurisdiction because the Constitution requires them to take recourse to specific remedy as provided in Article 117 of the Constitution before the Administrative Tribunal. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif; color: black;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><em><span style="color: black;">Majibur Rahman (Md) and ors </span></em><span style="color: black;">vs </span><em><span style="color: black;">'Secretary of Ministry of Social Welfare Government of the People's Republic of Bangladesh and others 7 BLC 120.</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><span style="color: black;">Section 6(1)—</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><em><span style="color: black;"> </span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><span style="color: black;">It is seen from the provision of section 6(1) of the Administrative Tribunal Act that an appeal lies from an order of the Administrative Tribunal. In the instant case the Administrative Tribunal refused the prayer for ad-interim order restraining the authority from granting promotion to the respondents. So the respondent Nos. 1-11 herein if were aggrieved by the order so passed by the Administrative Tribunal they were required as per provision of section 6(1) of the Administrative Tribunal Act to file appeal, if any, they would have thought fit. But instead of doing that they were not well advised to file the writ petition seeking the relief identical to the relief sought in the Administrative Tribunal case with the sole object of having an ad-interim order restraining the authority from taking steps for the promotion of the Assistant </span><span style="color: black;">Superintendent of Police to the post of Additional Superintendent of Police. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><em><span style="color: black;"> </span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><em><span style="color: black;">Khalilur Rahman, ASP SB, Dhaka vs Md Kamrul Ahsan 10 BLC (AD) 193.</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><em><span style="color: black;"> </span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><span style="color: black;">Section 6A—</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><em><span style="color: black;"> </span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif; color: black;">In the instant case PSC recommended for regularisation of the opposite parties No. 3-86 on 28-1-1998 and thereupon the said opposite parties became the members of the Bangladesh Civil Service (Enforcement: Police Cadre) and that being so in law they can only claim seniority in the Cadre Service on and from 28-1-1998 and no other date. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify; line-height: normal; background: white; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><strong><em><span style="color: black;"> </span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;"><em><span style="color: black;">Khalilur Rahman (Md) PPM and others vs Md Kamrul Ahsan and others 8 BLC (AD) 80.</span></em></span></p></div></div>
314	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Anti-Corruption Commission Act, 2004 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Citation:</b>  2 ALR(2013)(HCD) 201, 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 501,4 ALR 2014(2) 148, 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 88,5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 46,  3 ALR(2014)(1) 141,5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 260,5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 339,  5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 158, 2 ALR (2013)(AD) 109, 2 ALR (2013) (AD) 109,2 ALR (2013)</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2004</p><p><b>Subject:</b> class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 14.15pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 95.05pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Anti-Corruption Commission Act</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 14.15pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 95.05pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">         </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">         </span>[V of 2004]</span></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Truth and Accountability Commission (TAC)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">There is no qualm on the theme that the effects and consequences of a legislation or an Ordinance remain in force until it is subsequently declared invalid. It is a well-settled principle of law that a right or a privilege once vested in a man cannot be taken back. Therefore, the right to remain shielded from prosecution again for the same acts, was a valid right at the time it accrued to the petitioner by virtue of the presumption of validity. So, even though the Ordinance ceased to exist when it was declared ultra vires by a judgment of the High Court Division, yet the rights that stemmed from it during the period of its validity, cannot be erased. <em>Emon Shahriar -Vs- The State 2 ALR(2013)(HCD) 201</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 6(3) and 36</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The intent of the legislature in using of word "felt" in the ACC Act,2004 is to mean the date of joining in the work and, therefore, not the date of publication of any appointment order.Advocate Mirza AI Mahmood, Advocate -Vs-Mr. Golam Rahman and others 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 501</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.7pt 4.1pt .0001pt 1.5in;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: -7.7pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .95pt 0in .0001pt 7.7pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 18, 26 (1) and 27 Anti-Corruption Commission Rules, Rules 15 and 17</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When the notice was issued under sections 18 and 26(1) of the Anti Corruption Commission Act, 2004 read with Rule 15 (Gha) of the Emergency Power Rules 2007, admittedly on that date the Anti Corruption Commission was not in existence and as such the very issuance of notice is illegal and without jurisdiction. Md. Ariful Haque Chowdhury -Vs.-The State and others 4 ALR 2014(2) 148.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 2.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 26(2) and 27(2):- Concealment of property in the property statement and punishment for the same.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 5.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Since prima-facie there are materials against the petitioner attracting the ingredients of both the offences, the petitioner is under a legal obligation to clear his position and to account for possession of properties disproportionate to his known source of income. The onus is on the petitioner to rebut at the trial the presumption of guilt under section 27(2) of the Anti-Corruption Commission Act, 2004. Dr. Khandaker Mosharraf Hossain -Vs.- The State 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 88.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .7pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 26(2) and 33- Anticipatory Bail/pre-arrest Bail </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- It is an extra­ordinary remedy and an exception to the general rule of bail which can be granted only in extra-ordinary and exceptional circumstances upon a proper and intelligent exercise of discretion. The High Court Division cannot exercise its discretion whimsically at its suit will. The High Court Division has not properly exercised its discretion in granting the accused- respondent on anticipatory bail. We have given a cursory glance of the application for pre-arest bail. 'The grounds are also not relevant for the purpose of exercising discretion in the case. More so, the case having been filed by the Durnity Daman Commission in exercise of its power under Act of 2004, the Durnity Daman Commission is a necessary party but, the accused-respondent has not made it a party. Durnity Daman Commission. -Vs.-Jesmin Islam and another 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 46</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 26(2) and 33- Anticipatory Bail/pre-arrest Bail </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- It is an extra­ordinary remedy and an exception to the general rule of bail which can be granted only in extra-ordinary and exceptional circumstances upon a proper and intelligent exercise of discretion. The High Court Division cannot exercise its discretion whimsically at its suit will. The mission Act <strong><span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">[Vof2004]</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">High Court Division has not properly exercised its discretion in granting the accused- respondent on anticipatory bail. We have given a cursory glance of the application for pre-arest bail. 'The grounds are also not relevant for the purpose of exercising discretion in the case. More so, the case having been filed by the Durnity Daman Commission in exercise of its power under Act of 2004, the Durnity Daman Commission is a necessary party but, the accused-respondent has not made it a party. Durnity Daman Commission. -Vs.-Jesmin Islam and another 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 46.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 27(2) </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- It casts an allegation upon the accused to account for the disproportionate wealth. This section casts an obligation upon the accused to clear his position in respect of the questioned property and to account for the lawful possession thereof the accused cannot be let of in a summary proceeding.Mrs. Sabira Sultana - Vs.-The State and another 3 ALR(2014)(1) 141.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><strong>Section 28 read with </strong></span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Penal Code</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">[XLV of I860]</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 420 </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- ACC Act is a special statute having overriding effect over all other law now in force. The ACC Act and Rules framed there under provide for special procedure to examine the complaints, make inquiry, and investigation including provision for sanction before filing of charge-sheet and initiation of trial. Furthermore, jurisdiction of ordinary court to try the offences referred to in the Act is completely ousted and vested only in the Special Judge constituted under the Criminal Law Amendment Act, 1958. mere absence of jurisdiction does not absolve the accused of his criminal liability. He must face trial before a competent Court. Md. Altaf Hossain -Vs.- The State(Criminal) 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 260.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">]<strong>Section 28 </strong>read with </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Anti-Corruption Commission Rules, 2007, Rule 13(3)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It is crystal clear that it is only the Special Judge who is empowered under the law to accept a petition of complaint regarding any of the offences mentioned in the schedule of the ACC Ain under certain circumstances and to direct the ACC to investigate/inquire into the same. In the instant case the complaint was directly filed before the Court of the learned Chief Metropolitan Magistrate, Dhaka without following the provision of rule 13(3) of the ACC Rules and section 28 of the ACC Ain. Nawabjada Khaja Zaki Ahsanullah -Vs.- The State 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 339.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .25pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 28 </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- The jurisdiction of the writ Court to quash the proceedings of a criminal case unless the 'vires' of any law is found to have been challenged. Aggrieved person could have sought necessary remedies, if any, against the very initiation of the case which are available within the four corners of the relevant statute, that is to say, the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898.A.H.M. Aminul Islam -Vs.- Anti-Corruption Commission 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 158.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 0in .25pt .0001pt 1.5in;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .25pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 32 (1) - Further Investigating -</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Appellate Division held that the High Court Division observed that under section 173 (3 B) of the Code the Investigating Officer does not require any permission from the court concerned for further investigation and hence after completion of further investigation filing of supplementary charge sheet does not suffer from any illegality. The High Court Division has treated the subsequent investigation as a further investigation and the report as a supplementary charge sheet, which is not illegal Chowdhury Mohidul Haque -Vs.-Anti-Corruption Commission 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 71.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 32 Sub-sections 32(1) and 32(2).</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 1.2pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sanction for prosecution from the Anti -Corruption Commission is necessary for taking cognizance of an offence under the Act. The investigation officer is required under the law to obtain prior sanction of the Commission before submission of the charge-sheet after completing investigation and the charge-sheet must accompany charges under the amended provision of law, his prior sanction is necessary for filing a case.Anti-Corruption Commission -Vs.-Mohammad Bayazid 2 ALR (2013)(AD) 109.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sub-section 32(1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Before amendment of section 32(1) of the Anti-Corruption Commission (Amendment Ordinance, 2007) prior sanction from the Anti-Corruption Commission was a pre-condition for filing a case under this Act. Anti-Corruption Commission -Vs.-Mohammad Bayazid 2 ALR (2013) (AD) 109.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sub-section 32(2) Jn reamins unaffected by the Amendment of 2007.</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Under the amended provision the words' for filing<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>case'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>have<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>been deleted. Sanction for prosecution is Now necessary only for the purpose of taking cognizance or the offence. Prior sanction for filing a case under the Anti-Corruption Act as required before the Amendment is not now necessary .Anti-Corruption Commission -Vs.-Mohammad Bayazid 2 ALR (2013)(AD) 109</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"> </p></div></div>
315	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Anti-Corruption Commission Rules, 2007</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Citation:</b>  62 DLR 33, 62 DLR (AD) 290, 63 DLR 368, 62 DLR 20, 63 DLR 162, 63 DLR 368, 63 DLR 425,  61 DLR 772, 61 DLR 1,  63 DLR 294.</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Anti-Corruption Commission </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  1970-01-01</p><!DOCTYPE html><div style="text-align: justify;"> </div><div style="text-align: center;"><strong>Anti-Corruption Commission Rules, 2007</strong></div><div style="text-align: justify;"> <br/><strong>Rule 2—</strong>Inquiry and Investigation— ‘Inquiry’ and investigation’ are not one and the same. They are distinct terms. They are distinguishable from each other. Investigation (তদন্ত) of can only be commenced and carried out conclusion of inquiry (অনুসন্ধান) and lodgment of an FIR against a person. <em>Tofail Ahmed vs Chairman, Anti-Corruption Commission 62 DLR 33.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rules 3 &amp; 4—</strong>Words ‘মামলা দায়ের’ means institution of a case by submission of a charge-sheet by an officer of the Commission, before the concerned Court and certainly not an first information report as envisaged under section 154 the Code of Criminal Procedure or a complaint (অভিযোগ) as envisaged under Rule 3 and 4 of the Rules.<br/>The irresistible conclusion is that no sanction will be required to file a complaint (অভিযোগ) either with the Commission or with the police. But sanction from the Commission shall be required both under the unamended and the amended 32, before institution of a case “মামলা দায়েরের ক্ষেত্রে” in the concerned Court. <em>Anti-Corruption Commission vs Dr Mohiuddin Khan Alamgir</em> <em>62 DLR (AD) 290.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rule 3 &amp; 4—</strong>An officer of the Commission lodged a first information report on 6-3-2007 with the Tejgaon Police Station and a case started. This is not envisaged under rules 3and 4 of the Rules. Those Rules provide only for filing of the complaint involving the offences mentioned in the schedule to the Act. However, those provisions are merely directory and deviation from provisions in lodging an first information report instead of a complaint, would not vitiate the proceedings. <em>Anti-Corruption vs Dr Mohiuddin Khan Alamgir 62 DLR (AD) 290.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rules 3 &amp; 4—</strong>Commissioners resigned from the Commission on 7-2-2007 and it was reconstituted on 24-2-2007, as such, although the Commission existed as an Institution on 18-2-2007, when the notice was issued, but there was no Commission within the meaning of section 3 read with section 5 of the Act on that date. <em>Anti-Corruption Commission vs Dr Mohiuddin Khan Alamgir 62 DLR (AD) 290.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rules 4 and 16—</strong>Rule 16 of the Anti- Corruption Commission Rules, 2007 is applicable only in the case of any officer of the Anti-Corruption Commissioner, who lay the trap and conduct the trap operation only. This provision of law being a special law like Anti-Corruption Commission Rule, 2007 or Section 20 or 17 of the Anti- Corruption Commission Act, 2004 did not oust the jurisdiction of other law enforcing agencies. Occurrence took place on 23-1-2011 and FIR was lodged on 24-1-2011 and on the same day it was transmitted to the Anti-Corruption Commission for investigation following the procedure of Rule 4 of the Anti-Corruption Commission Rule, 2007. <em>SM Sabbir Hasan vs State 63 DLR 368.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rules 7(1)(2) &amp; 17(1)—</strong>A well-established legal principle is that a person upon whom power is delegated cannot delegate the same to another person. In the instant case the legal provision in Rule 17(1) is such that the Commission itself could delegate the power to issue a notice for submission of wealth statement to anyone of its officers not below the rank of Deputy Director (DD). <em>Akbar Khan vs ACC 62 DLR 20.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rules 8 and 15—</strong>ACC did never wanted to know it by affording the petitioner an opportunity of being heard or by calling for a written statement from him, which it had power to under Rule 8 and II of the ACC Rules, 2007. Such discretion is neither unfettered, nor it has been vested in the ACC to arm it with redundant power or to exercise its discretion with caprice, but be guided by the provisions of section 3(2) of the Act. <em>Obaidul Kader (Md) vs State 63 DLR 425.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rule 10—</strong>In respect of submission of charge-sheet and its requirement for sanction the learned Counsel submits that sub-rule (1) of Rule 15 to 18 of the Anti-Corruption rules speaks about the sanction and filing of the case and charge- sheet thereto. The sanction as given by one of the Commissioner of the Commission to submit charge-sheet purported to have been signed by one of the Commissioner of the Commission is not at all valid sanction, as he did not apply his mind to the requirement of the law and the materials available on record. Even, he did not go through the 161 and 164 statements of the witnesses at all. Having been done so he ought to have refused to accord sanction. In short, it may be called that the alleged sanction is a mechanical sanction and it did not fulfill the requirement of the law rather it is contrary to decisions of the Apex Courts and, as such, taking of cognizance on such charge-sheet is illegal, malafide which amounts to a malice in law. <em>Sheikh Hasina vs State 63 DLR 162.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rule 10—</strong>The Court below has seen the CD and became sure about the transaction. The matter is still under investigation and if the mighty accused is granted bail the investigation of the case will be hampered as he holds very powerful position in the Anti-Corruption Commission. <em>SM Sabbir Hasan vs State 63 DLR 368.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rule 11—</strong>The act of the Commission in according the sanction, without affording the accused any hearing under Rule 11 of the ACC Rules, 2007, amounts to colorable exercise of power by the ACC and its failure to remain স্বাধীন ও নিরপেক্ষ which is the touch stone to judge the validity of its acts and deeds. <em>Obaidul Kader vs State 63 DLR 425.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rule 15—</strong>A valid sanction being a condition precedent to a valid prosecution, The impugned proceeding has been launched without a valid sanction and the same, based on such a sanction amounts to an abuse of the process of the Court. <em>Obaidul Kader vs State 63 DLR 425.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rules 15 &amp; 16—</strong>The sanction in question has not been accorded as per prescribed Form-3, mandatorily required by rule 15(7), and that apparently the same has been given mechanically. Hence the questioned sanction is not a sanction in the eye of law. <em>Bayazid vs State 61 DLR 772.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rule 15(7)—</strong>Form 3—”Form 3” is the part of the statute and accordingly when a specified Form has been prescribed in the statute for particular purpose the sanctioning authority has no scope to assign any reason of its satisfaction beyond the said format given in the form. <em>Habibur Rahman Molla vs State 61 DLR 1.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rule 15(7)—</strong>Form 3—There is no scope to challenge the efficacy of the sanction which has been accorded in Form No. 3 under rule 15(7) of the ACC Rules, 2007 prescribed by the legislature. The recital of the sanction order clearly shows that sanctioning authority was satisfied, on scrutinizing the record, produced in respect of the allegation brought against the accused-petitioner to accord sanction for prosecution. <em>Habibur Rahman Molla vs State 61 DLR 1.</em><br/> <br/><strong>Rule 16(2)—</strong>Neither the seizure list witness PWs 4 and 5 nor the PWs 9, 10 and 11 who<br/>accompanied with PW 1 did support the prosecution case in respect of recovery of marks notes from the possession of the appellants. Rather the defence case was that due to fail in the Dispute Case No. 129 of 2003 on 2-7-2003 out of the grudge PW 8 Abul Kalam Azad who proved himself as a ‘Mamlabaz’ subsequently created a false case against the accused-appellants with the help of PW 1 who without taking any effective permission as per Rule 16(2) of the Anti-Corruption Commission Rule brought the case is more probable. <em>Jahangir Alam vs State 63 DLR 294.</em><br/> </div></div></div>
316	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Appellate Division Rules,1988 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Citation:</b>  6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)95. 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)224, 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)67, </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  1988</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Appellate Division Rules,1988 </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2018-05-29</p><!DOCTYPE html><p><!-- [if gte mso 9]><xml> <o:OfficeDocumentSettings>  <o:RelyOnVML/>  <o:AllowPNG/> </o:OfficeDocumentSettings></xml><![endif]--></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 11.3pt .7pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">                                             Appellate Division Rules,1988 </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 11.3pt .7pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Order XXVI rules 1-6</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 11.3pt .7pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Appellate Division held that the procedures provided in Order XXVI rules 1-6 of the Appellate Division Rules, which are not inconsistent with the Act and the Rules, would guide the procedure and practice of the Appellate Division for disposal of a review petition, that is to say, a review in a criminal matter can be made on the ground of an error apparent on the face of the record, <em>Muhammad Kamaruzzaman -Vs.-Chief Prosecutor, International Crimes Tribunal </em></span><br/><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><em>6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)95.</em></span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Appellate Division is of the view making some discrepant statements only their whole evidence should not be discarded and they also should not be treated as untrustworthy.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The number of accused is more than hundred. Hundreds of people were present in the place of occurrence and witnessed this occurrence. In the circumstances it was difficult to pinpoint specifically the role played by each and every accused. So it is most natural that there may occur some discrepancies in the evidence of the prosecution witnesses as to the role played by the accused persons in this occurrence. While sifting the evidence of the prosecution witnesses the courts are to take into consideration the discrepancies also in their evidence, but for making some discrepant statements only their whole evidence should not be discarded and they also should not be treated as untrustworthy<em> Shafiul Azam Dafader-Vs.-The State 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)224.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Appellate Division comments about the impugned judgment of the High Court Division.</span></strong></p><p class="Style11" style="margin-top: .25pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; line-height: normal; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The High Court Division, without making any discussion of any evidence at all and without adverting to the findings and decision and the reasoning thereof made by the appellate court below, set aside the judgment and decree of the appellate court below-the last court of fact. The High Court Division did not bother even to make any reasoning as to why it set aside the judgment of the appellate court below. When the High Court Division, in When the High Court Division, in exercising its revisional jurisdiction, concurs with the findings and decision made by the appellate court below it (High Court Division) may not make elaborate discussion of the evidence on record, but even then also it must give reasoning’s of its concurring with the findings and decision of the appellate court below. In the present case the High Court Division set aside the judgment and decree of the appellate court below without making any discussion of the evidence on record and without giving any reasoning at all of doing so. Appellate Division, with high dissatisfaction, deprecate writing of this sort of judgments by the High Court Division. <em>Md. Shamezuddin -Vs.- Md. Nowsher AH Fakir 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)67.</em></span></p><p> </p></div></div>
317	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Arm Act, 1872</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Citation:</b>   1 ALR (HCDJ109, 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 323, 4 ALR (AD) 2014 (2) 125, 4 ALR 2014(2) 351. . 4 ALR 2014(2) 70, 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 28, 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)95.   </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  1878</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Arm Act</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2018-05-29</p><!DOCTYPE html><p><!-- [if gte mso 9]><xml> <o:OfficeDocumentSettings>  <o:RelyOnVML/>  <o:AllowPNG/> </o:OfficeDocumentSettings></xml><![endif]--></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-bidi-language: BN-BD;">                                                           Arm Act</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-bidi-language: BN-BD;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                             </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                           </span>[X of 1878]</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 19A and 19(f) Evidence Act </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; font-variant: small-caps;">[<strong>i </strong></span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'MS Mincho';">of 1872]</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 114(g)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 2.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">As for the present case, it appears that neither the seizure list witnesses nor the local witnesses were examined by the prosecution. In the context of the fact of cited case, relating to corroboration appears to be distinguishable from the present case. Under the circumstances there is no hesitation in holding that the prosecution has totally failed to prove the recovery of the arms and bullet from the exclusive control and possession of the petitioner. It appears that non-examination of important witnesses creates presumption under section 114(g) of the Evidence Act and raises doubt about the prosecution case and benefit of doubt would always go in favour of the accused petitioner. The prosecution has miserably failed to prove recovery of arms and bullet from the exclusive control and possession of the petitioner by adducing reliable and independent evidence before the Tribunal. The impugned judgment and order is quashed.<em>@ Galcuta Hanif andHanif.-Vs-The State 1 ALR (HCDJ109.</em></span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                 </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 19 A Evidence Act </span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">[I of 1872]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 114 (g) </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- Evidentiary value of the deposition of police personnel. - There is no reason to disbelieve the P.W's 1-4 only because they are police personnel when there is no contradiction or discrepancy rather consistency in their deposition. <em>Jahangir Alam -Vs.- The State 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 152</em></span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                  </span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 19A - "Bail" application pending investigation under the Arms Act</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">According to the FIR arms were recovered from a co- accused's house after the petitioner's disclosure. The case is still in the investigative stage. The High Court Division are not, hence, poised to enlarge the petitioner on bail at this stage. <em>J amir Uddin - Vs.- The State 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 323</em></span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">          </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">               </span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 19A and 19(f)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">All the witnesses in a chorus corroborated the prosecution case that the arms were recovered as per showing of the two confessing accused and the confessional statements corroborated other materials on record. And such the submission for the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>petitioners<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>that<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>arms and ammunition in question were not recovered from the direct possession of the ssused person and the confessional statements of two accused perons are exclupatory in nature merit no consideration. <em>Kazi Kamrul and others-Vs.-The State. 4 ALR (AD) 2014 (2) 125.</em></span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                   </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><br/></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 19A and 19(f)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: .7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It transpires that the evidence of all the prosecution witnesses in respect of recovery of the arms from the convict-appellants are consistent, uniform and corroborative with each other in respect of all materials particulars. There is absolutely no reason to disbelieve the consistent and corroborative evidence of those competent witnesses having no reason whatsoever to depose falsely against the appellants.<em>Abdul Azid alias Azid Dacoit -Vs.-The State. 4 ALR 2014(2) 351.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 19A and l9(f)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.1pt 1.45pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The High Court Division found that there is no positive evidence on record in order to prove that the alleged arms and ammunitions were recovered from the exclusive control and possession of the convict-petitioner and the same were kept by him at the place of occurrence thus the Court quashed and order. <em>Md. Iqbal Hossain Bhuiyan -Vs.- The State. 4 ALR 2014(2) 70.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Appointment of Special Judge</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Notification vide Circular dated 04.03.2014, was made promoting and transferring/ appointing respondent No. 4 and another Special Judge, Dhaka along with 19 other Judicial Officers. The Act, 1958, did not anywhere require that a special and separate Circular/ Gazette Notification has to be made for appointment of any Special Judge, as such, High Court found no substance in the submission of the learned Advocate for the petitioner that the Gazette Notification dated 08.05.2014, is not a proper Gazette Notification in the eye of law as per Act, 1958. It must also be taken into account that. <em>Begum Khaleda Zia -Vs.-Government of Bangladesh and others 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 28.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">A review is maintainable from the judgment of the Appellate Division subject to the condition that where the error is so apparent and patent that review is necessary to avoid miscarriage of justice: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">judicial fallibility. Power of review is not an inherent power - it must be conferred by law either specifically or by necessary implication and that despite there being no provision in the Act or the Rules for review from the judgment of the Appellate Division on appeal, by fiction of law a review is maintainable from the judgment of the Appellate Division subject to the condition that where the error is so apparent and patent that review is necessary to avoid miscarriage of justice.<em> Muhammad Kamaruzzaman -Vs.-Chief Prosecutor, International Crimes Tribunal 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)95</em><strong>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></strong></span></p><p> </p></div></div>

class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .25pt 0in .0001pt 30.25pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">                        Bankers Books Evidence Act</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.45pt .7pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                        </span>Code of Criminal Procedure</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .5pt .7pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                       </span>(V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section - 94(l)(b)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Court has power to call for any paper or document in possession of any person, including Banking institutions, for its production before it, which is considered necessary for a proper trial of the case before it. The Court has also the power to summon any person to appear before it and to depose in the case when his evidence is considered necessary for a proper trial and that in the interest of justice. In the instant case the production of the relevant bank document is vitally necessary for proof of the complainant's case and as such the learned Magistrate was not at all justified in refusing to call for the necessary Bank document and refusing to summon the local Sonali Bank Manager as a witness in the case. The learned Magistrate is directed to cause production of the necessary band papers for the purpose of the trial by following the provisions of the Bankers, Books Evidence Act, 1891.<em>Juboraj Goula -Vs.- The State 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 175.</em></span></p></div></div>
