<w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="39" QFormat="true" Name="TOC Heading"/> </w:LatentStyles></xml><![endif]--><!-- [if gte mso 10]><style> /* Style Definitions */ table.MsoNormalTable	{mso-style-name:"Table Normal";	mso-tstyle-rowband-size:0;	mso-tstyle-colband-size:0;	mso-style-noshow:yes;	mso-style-priority:99;	mso-style-qformat:yes;	mso-style-parent:"";	mso-padding-alt:0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;	mso-para-margin-top:0in;	mso-para-margin-right:0in;	mso-para-margin-bottom:10.0pt;	mso-para-margin-left:0in;	line-height:115%;	mso-pagination:widow-orphan;	font-size:11.0pt;	mso-bidi-font-size:14.0pt;	font-family:"Angsana New","serif";	mso-hansi-font-family:Calibri;	mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;	mso-bidi-language:BN;}</style><![endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">                                              Constitution of Bangladesh</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                              </span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> Article 102</span></strong></p><p><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                               </span>Penal Code </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: 1.0pt;">[XLV of 1860]</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: 1.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 154</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.45pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Police Regulation of Bengal Regulation 252</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In view of the provisions of section 154 of the Penal Code and regulation 252 of the Police Regulation of Bengal the sub-inspector of police in the garb of <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span><strong>Bangla Type Here</strong> issued the impugned notice upon the petitioner restraining him from enjoying the land in question by directing the petitioner to stop further construction on the case land and also to maintain status-quo is ex-facie without jurisdiction. Moreso, since it is a non-cognizable offence permission from the Judicial Magistrate concerned is also required to be procured. <em>Md. Kodor Ali,-Vs-Additional Deputy Commissioner (Revenue) Sylhet and others 1 ALR (HCD) 41</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.45pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Constitution of Bangladesh Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The petitioner in the instant case has invoked writ jurisdiction under Article 102 of the Constitution of the People's Republic of Bangladesh challenging the impugned proceeding seeking equitable relief, but without surrendering before the Court of law. He being fugitive is debarred from seeking any relief before this Court. Accordingly, this Rule is liable to be discharged as being not maintainable.<em>Md. Shamsur Rashid Majnu-Vs-Anti-Corruption Commission and others 1 ALR (HCD) 129.</em></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 10.55pt .95pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Constitution of Bangladesh</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.9pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Article 102 - No scope for quashing in writ-jurisdiction unless the vires of the law involved is challenged.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">There is no scope for quashing a criminal proceeding under the writ-jurisdiction unless the vires of the law involved is challenged. Having gone through the rule issuing order, the Appellate Division finds that the vires of the law involved in the present case has not been challenged. Therefore, there is no scope for aggrandizement of jurisdiction of the High Court Division in quashing a criminal proceeding. Consequently, the High Court Division was not justified in quashing 15 criminal cases (Special Case f Bangladesh Nos. 12-26 of 2007) in exercise of its power under Article 102 of the Constitution. <em>The Anti-Corruption Commission -Vs.- Mehadi Hasan 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 105.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                            </span></span></em><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Constitution of Bangladesh</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Article 102- Writ jurisdiction cannot invoke challenging the criminal case.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .15in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Anti-Corruption Commission Act </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">(V of 2004)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 28 </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- The jurisdiction of the writ Court to quash the proceedings of a criminal case unless the 'vires' of any law is found to have been challenged. Aggrieved person could have sought necessary remedies, if any, against the very initiation of the case which are available within the four corners of the relevant statute, that is to say, the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898.<em>A.H.M. Aminul Islam -Vs.- Anti-Corruption Commission 5 ALR (HCD)2015(I) 158.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .25pt; text-indent: 32.9pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                   </span>Constitution of Bangladesh Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Writ Petitioner challenged Motijheel PS case Nos. 77 and 79 both dated 28.12.2006 </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Accused petitioner earlier challenged Motijheel<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>PS<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>case<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>No.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>89 dated28.12.2006 in Writ Petition No. 450 of 2007 but ultimately the rule was discharged. An ad-interim order of stay was passed at the time of issuance of the Rule in connection with Motijheel PS case No. 79 of 2006. Now the same Petitioner has filed the instant Writ Petition Nos. 7228 of 2010 and 7227 of 2010, challenging the Motijheel PS Case Nos. being. 77 and 79, dated 28.12.2006, mainly praying for a direction for expeditious conclusion of the investigation of the said cases. In view of the fact that the accused -Petitioner's earlier Writ Petition No. 450 of 2007 challenging Motijheel PS case No. 79 of 2006 has already been discharged and in view of the fact that the two cases are now pending in the Court of the Chief Metropolitan Magistrate, Dhaka the present rules have become redundant. The Rules are discharged as being in fructuous. <em>Md. Azam-E-Sadat - Vs- Anti-Corruption Commission 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 81.</em></span></p><p><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .5pt .25pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Constitution of Bangladesh</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Article 103 (2) (c) - Contempt of Court</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Three broad categories of contempt namely (1) scandalisation of the court, (2) disobedience to the orders of the court and breach of undertakings given to the court and (3) interference with the due course of justice. Appellate Division observes that the news report published in<em> f Bangladesh </em>the daily Bhorer Kagoj, impugned before the High Court Division, certainly had the effect of scandalizing the justice delivery system However, upon careful, scrutiny of the full reports Appellate Division inclined to accept that the report in the daily Prothom Alo does not by itself have the effect of scandalizing the concerned Judge or the judiciary. What the report does, in fact, is bring into focus scandals involved in the tabulation sheets of examination marks by the Chittagong University. However, the report by the Bhorer Kagoj goes further than a simple narration of the inquiry and findings with regard to the manipulation of marks in the tabulation sheets by the office of the Controller of Examination of Chittagong University and gives the personal opinion of the reporter as to what effect the corruption, forgery, interpolation etc. brings upon the judiciary when such persons whose examination results are manipulated are appointed as Judges of the Supreme Court. This would clearly have a negative effect on the minds of the general public and undermine their confidence in the justice delivery system.<em> Ekramul Haque Balbul -Vs.-Muhammad Faiz 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 109.</em></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Constitution of Bangladesh</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.5pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Article 104 read with</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 2.9pt; text-indent: 46.3pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                        </span>Penal Code </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 2.9pt; text-indent: 46.3pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                       </span>[<span style="font-variant: small-caps; letter-spacing: .5pt;">xlv </span>of 1860] </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.5pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 406/409/420/460 and 469 and</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                              </span>Prevention of Corruption Act</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">[II of 1947] </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><strong>Section 5(2)</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Appellate Division on scrutiny of the materials on record took the view that the allegations imputed by the complainant against the appellant that they had been misappropriated the awarded amount are not at all tenable and as such Appellate Division exercised the power under Article 104 of the constitutions for doing complete justice from unnecessary for the avowed purpose of protecting the appellants from the unnecessary hassle of criminal proceeding as there was no material to prosecute them. <em>Mahboobur Rahman and others -Vs.-Md. Kayser Parvej (Milon) and others. 4 ALR (AD) 2014 (2) 149.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Confession of two accuseds recorded by the Magistrate was gap of 30 minutes whether admissible!</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The High Court Division observed that the duty of filling up of the columns of the prescribed form of the confession is a routine duty and the actual confession of each of the confessing accused consists of a few lines and since the confessions are not voluminous, a man of ordinary prudence will be led to hold that the gap of 30 minutes is sufficient for recording the confession of the confessing accused concerned by the Magistrate. On this count, High Court Division does not find any fault. <em>Md. Uzzal Hossain and others -Vs-The State 6 ALR - 2015(2)269.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.2pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Credibility of testimony oral and circumstantial, depends considerably on a judicial evaluation of the totality, not isolated scrutiny. When dealing with the serious question of guilt or innocence of persons charged with crime, the following principles should be taken into consideration.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 0in; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 42.5pt; margin: 11.3pt 0in .0001pt 0in;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The onus of proving everything essential to the establishment of the charge against the accused lies on the prosecutor.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 0in; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 42.5pt; margin: 9.85pt 0in .0001pt 0in;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The evidence must be such asto exclude to a moral certainty every reasonable doubt of the guilt of the accused.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 0in; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 42.5pt; margin: 7.7pt 0in .0001pt 0in;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In matters of doubt it is safer to acquit than to condemn, for it is better that several guilty persons should escape than that one innocent person suffer.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 0in; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 42.5pt; margin: 11.3pt 0in .0001pt 0in;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">d)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">There must be clear and unequivocal proof of the corpus delicit.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 0in; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 42.5pt; margin: 11.3pt 0in .0001pt 0in;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">e)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The hypothesis of delinquency should be consistent with all the facts proved.</span></em></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Munna Dey - Vs.- The State 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 147</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.5pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Circumstantial evidence</span></strong></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">There is no ocular evidence witnessing the commission of crime by convict-appellant. Prosecution relied upon circumstantial evidence in proof of its case. It is always to be remembered that there is no law that commission of a crime must by witnessed by witnesses and they are to stand in witness box to prove the crime. Commission of crime can be also, well proved by circumstantial evidence. Circumstantial evidence is more cogent and convincing than the ocular evidence. It is correctly said that witnesses may tell a lie and it is not difficult to procure false, tutored and biased witness but it was very much difficult to procure circumstantial evidence. <em>The State -Vs.- Belial Hossain 5 ALR(HCD)2015(1) 284.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Circumstances that justify commutation of death sentence.</span></strong></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In view of the facts that the condemned -prisoner is comparatively young in age with no previous criminal record, and in the back drone of admitted strained relationship between the parties. Compiled with the fact that he had languished in the condemned cell for more than 812 years, always under the sceptre of death, the Appellate Division considered these mitigating circumstances as sufficient to meet the ends of justice by is commuting the sentence of death into to one of imprisonment for life. <em>RahmatAlialiasShukkur- Vs. - The State 2 ALR(2013)(AD) 254</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In case of any conflict between the parent law and the rules framed there under, the parent law shall prevail over the rules. Rules made under a statute must be treated as a part of the main section, with no additional or independent connotation. A sub-ordinate or delegated authority has no power to transcend the power given or delegated to it by the parent authority.<em>Anti-Corruption Commission -Vs.-Mohammad Bayazid 2 ALR (2013)(AD) 109.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.25pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">A criminal offence never abates It is never barred by limitation.(Para.25)</span></strong></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">A Judicial officer is expected to perform his judicial work cautiously, diligently and in accordance with law, fully applying his judicial mind into the facts and circumstances of the case and the evidence on record, without depending on the Public Prosecutor or defence lawyer.<em>Md. Iftekharul Karim -Vs.- The State 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 470.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.25pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                          </span>Cruelty to Women (Deterrent Punishment) Ordinance, 1983</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0.5pt 0in 0.0001pt 46.55pt; text-indent: -46.55pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 4 (Kha) and 10 read with <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0.5pt 0in 0.0001pt 46.55pt; text-indent: -46.55pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">       </span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0.5pt 0in 0.0001pt 46.55pt; text-indent: -46.55pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                           </span>Penal Code [</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; font-variant: small-caps; letter-spacing: .5pt;">xlv </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">of 1860<strong>]</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 376</span></strong></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The process of sentencing is at the discretion of the Judge and is at the same time circumscribed by the law. It transpires that the respondent was in custody during the pendency of the appeal from 1993 to 2001 and, therefore, served a term of imprisonment of about 8 years. The High Court Division took the view that the period served by the respondent was sufficient to meet the ends of justice. The appellate Division does not find any illegality in the impugned judgment and, therefore, finds no reason to interfere with the impugned judgment and order.<em>The State -Vs.-Md. Shamsur Rahman Sikder @ Kalu &amp; others. 4 ALR (AD) 2014 (2) 42.</em></span></p></div></div>
324	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">  Criminal Law Amendment Act, 1958</h2>

Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                  </span>Criminal Law Amendment Act, 1958</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.5pt; 10(1A)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 9.6pt 2.65pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Power to direct further investigation by the Special Judge and revisional power of the High Court Division under section 10(1A) of the Act.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Criminal Law Amendment Act, 1958 being a Special law, it prevails over the General provisions of the Code of Criminal Procedure. The Divisional Special Judge has jurisdiction to direct further investigation of a case before framing of charges whenever it appears to him to be proper under given circumstances. In our case under review, the learned Divisional Special Judge is found to have rightly exercised his power in directing further investigation into the case and it calls for no interference by High court Division in the exercise of its revitional power under section 10(1 A) of the Criminal Law Amendment Act, 1958. <em>Md. Amirul Karim -Vs.- The State 2ALR(2013)(HCD) 411.</em></span></p></div></div>

justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">                                                Customs Act, 1969</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 5.75pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">                                                      [IV of 1969]</span></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 19 and 32 </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- The provision has no connection with the import of goods under the baggage rules. The relevant rules under consideration are the Passenger (Non-tourist) Baggage (Import) Rules, 2000. Quite clearly, the rules apply generally to goods imported by passengers. <em>The State - Vs.- Md. Manzurul Alam 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 29.\</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.9pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Criminal Trial</span></strong></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Trial Court should issue summons or warrants to ensure the presence of the witnesses. <em>Ruhul Amin<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>-Vs.- <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>The<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>State 3 ALR(2014)(1) 157 .</em></span></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Cross Examination</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Failure to cross- examine a witness tantamount to admitting the evidence.<em>The State-Vs.-Alam @ Md. Alam and others 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 517.</em></span></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></em><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Difference between cheating and breach of contract</span></strong></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In every case of cheating there is implicit agreement between the parties. The vital factor to be considered is whether at the time of agreement there was intention to carry out the terms of the contract or not. If there is nothing to show that there was no intention at the time of agreement which was arrived at, but the failure to fulfill the terms of the agreement was the subsequent event, the offence of cheating cannot be said to have been committed. It would only be a case of breach of contract. <em>Prof. Dr. Motior Rahman-Vs.-The State and another 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)181.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Disputed question of facts can be decided only on evidence.</span></strong></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Before disposal of his application for discharge and framing of charge by the trial Court, the petitioner moved the High Court Division for quashing the criminal proceeding. The High Court Division discharged the Rule holding that a disputed question of fact can only be decided on taking evidence. The Appellate Division upheld the decition of the High Court Division and dismissed the petition. <em>Md. Mofizur Rahman -Vs.- The State 1 ALR (AD) 221.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Doctor opinion and victim's statement as to age are no proof of age.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Doctor's certificate as to age of the victim at 171/2-181/2 years of age, doctor's opinion as to the age is no conclusive proof thereof and the declaration in the statement under section 164 Cr.P.C. of the victim that she was a major are no proof of age and that radiologist's opinion cannot be preferred to positive evidence like school certificate. <em>Arun Karmakar -Vs.- The State 3 ALR(2014)(1)(AD) 222.</em></span></p></div></div>

<w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="63" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Shading 1 Accent 6"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="64" SemiHidden="false" Name="Medium Grid 1 Accent 6"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="68" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 2 Accent 6"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="69" <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="71" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Shading Accent 6"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="72" SemiHidden="false" Locked="false" Priority="19" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" QFormat="true" Name="Subtle Emphasis"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="21" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" QFormat="true" Name="Intense Emphasis"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="31" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" QFormat="true" Name="Subtle Reference"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="32" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" QFormat="true" Name="Intense Reference"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="33" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" QFormat="true" Name="Book Title"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="37" Name="Bibliography"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="39" QFormat="true" Name="TOC Heading"/> </w:LatentStyles></xml><![endif]--><!-- [if gte mso 10]><style> /* Style Definitions */ table.MsoNormalTable	{mso-style-name:"Table Normal";	mso-tstyle-rowband-size:0;	mso-tstyle-colband-size:0;	mso-style-noshow:yes;	mso-style-priority:99;	mso-style-qformat:yes;	mso-style-parent:"";	mso-padding-alt:0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;	mso-para-margin-top:0in;	mso-para-margin-right:0in;	mso-para-margin-bottom:10.0pt;	mso-para-margin-left:0in;	line-height:115%;	mso-pagination:widow-orphan;	font-size:11.0pt;	mso-bidi-font-size:14.0pt;	font-family:"Calibri","sans-serif";	mso-ascii-font-family:Calibri;	mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;	mso-hansi-font-family:Calibri;	mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;}</style><![endif]--><!-- [if gte mso 9]><xml> <o:shapedefaults v:ext="edit" spidmax="1027"/></xml><![endif]--><!-- [if gte mso 9]><xml> <o:shapelayout v:ext="edit">  <o:idmap v:ext="edit" data="1"/> </o:shapelayout></xml><![endif]--></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .7in; text-indent: 105.6pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Evidence Act </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">[I of 1872]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 3.1pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">3</span></p><p class="Style7" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The facts proved by the prosecution lead no inference of guilt of the appellants. The inference of guilt can only be drawn if the proved facts are consistent with the guilt of the appellants and inconsistent wholly with their innocence. The prosecution has totally failed to lead evidence to draw such inference against them. (Per S.K. Sinha, J minority view).<em>Sree Rabindra Nath Roy @ Rabindra and another -Vs- The State 1 ALR (AD) 189.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 5.3pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">3 <strong>and 105</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">At the earliest point of time those witnesses did not disclose the material facts either to the Investigating Officer or to the locals which makes the prosecution case shaky. It is well settled that when an eye witness to the occurrence that took does not disclose the names of the assailants he allegedly recognized and other material facts to the witnesses who came to the scene immediately after the occurrence was over or at the earliest opportunity and there is no justifiable reason for non discloser of the material facts, belated discloser of material facts renders their evidence/ testimony doubtful. In such a case the Court should reasonably infer that the story of recognition of the assailants was a subsequent embellishment. It is also well settled that when an eye witness witnessed the occurrence, accused person departed from the scene and many people assembled at the place of occurrence followed by officials it is expected that the eye witnesses will name the accused persons not only to their own kith and kin but also to uninvolved persons, including high officials. Belated discloser of the names of the assailants and of material facts make their evidence doubtful. <em>The State -Vs- Pannu &amp; others 1 ALR(2012) (HCD) 87.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 5.3pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 8</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It appears from the facts and circumstances and evidence on record that although the fact of the alleged murder was discovered by accused Siraj and the members of his family at about 9.00 hours but till 10.00 hours in that morning this fact was not informed to the parents of the deceased Sabrina Afroz Julie which also gives rise to doubt as to the conduct and demeanor of Siraj and his sons Sohel and Rajib. The above demeanor and subsequent conduct of the condemned prisoners Siraj, Sohel and Rajib are admissible in evidence under Section 8 of the Evidence Act.<em>The State -Vs.- Md. Sirajul Islam and others 1 ALR(2012) (HCD) 185.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 8</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Circumstantial evidence may be and frequently is more cogent than the evidence of eye-witnesses. It is not difficult to produce false evidence of eye witnesses. It is, on the other hand, extremely difficult to produce circumstantial evidence of a convincing character and, therefore, circumstantial evidence, if convincing, is more cogent than the evidence of eye witnesses.<em>The State -Vs.- Md. Sirajul Islam and others 1 ALR(2012) (HCD)185.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 8</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 8.4pt 0.7pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">By judicial pronouncements it is now settled that if the circumstantial evidence is far from satisfactory and it suffers from a number of infirmity, the court is left with no option other than to acquit the accused. If two infirmities are possible from the circumstantial evidence, one pointing to the guilt of the accused and the other also plausible, that the commission of the crime was the act of some one else, the circumstantial evidence would not warrant conviction of the accused. (Per S.K. Sinha, J minority view). <em>Sree Rabindra Rabindra <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Nath Roy @ Vs State and another 1 ALR (AD) 189.</em></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0.5pt 1.2pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 8.4pt 0.7pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 8 and 9, Circumstantial evidence a regardey positive from justice. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 8.4pt 0.7pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Convict after getting bail went to hiding and did not face trial and without offering any explanation as to why he avoided trial of the case. Further, convict even did not prefer any appeal challenging the judgment and order by which he has been convicted and sentenced or surrender before the Court. This conduct of the said convict is a relevant fact which should be taken into consideration as a circumstance in determining his guilt as per the provision of section 8 and 9 of Evidence Act, 1872 . A fugitive from justice defying the process of the Court without submitting to the due process of the Court is not entitled to obtain any judicial order in his aid showing leniency. The State - Vs. Asab Uddin 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 35</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.5pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 8</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 8.4pt 0.7pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It has been held in a number of cases that even an innocent man may feel paniky and may try to evade arrest when wrongly suspected of a grave crime; such is the instinct of self-preservation. The fact of absconding is no doubt a relevant piece of evidence to be considered along with other evidence but its value would always depend on circumstances of each case. (Per S.K. Sinha, J minority view).<em>Sree Rabindra Nath Roy @ Rabindra and another -Vs-The State 1 ALR (AD) 189</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.5pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 11, 32 and 137</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 8.4pt 0.7pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Tribunal has no basic conception of law on the point of admissibility of a statement made by a witness before a police officer which does not fall within the terms of section 32 of the Evidence Act. It cannot be held relevant under section 11 of the Evidence Act. If the maker of a statement is examined as a witness, ordinarily his previous statement is admissible merely to corroborate or contradict the testimony in Court but it cannot be taken as substantive evidence. The learned Judge illegally drew adverse inference against the defence observing that the appellants failed to establish by cross-examining her that the statement was false. (Per S.K.Sinha,J minority view).<em>Sree Rabindra Nath Roy @ Rabindra and another -Vs- The State 1 ALR (AD) 189.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 8.4pt 0.7pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.5pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 24 and 30</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 8.4pt 0.7pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The inculpatory confessional statements of the condemned prisoners Jamir and Piyas as well as of accused Babul Miah (since deceased) corroborated by the attending circumstances and material evidence are sufficient to establish beyond any reasonable doubt that all the appellants Siraj, Rajib, Sohel, Masum, Kabir, Piyas, Jamir and Manik and another Babul Miah (since deceased) pursuant to a conspiracy in furtherance of their common intention of all brutally committed the murder of Akhter Hossain, his wife Sabrina Afroz Julie and their daughter Arna Akhter aged about 2/4 years. There is also nothing to show as to why would the confessing accused persons Jamir, Piyas and Babul Miah (since deceased) falsely assigned part of killing to the other co-accused persons Siraj, Rajib, Sohel, Masum and Kabir. <em>The State -Vs.- Md. Sirajul Islam and others 1 ALR (HCD)185.</em></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0.7pt 1.9pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.5pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 27</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 8.4pt 0.7pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It has been consistently stated by the confessing accused persons in their confessional statements that at least two daos including one Ram Dao, two Shafals and instrument for breaking grill were used in the commission of the alleged offence which they, after committing the alleged offence threw in the nearby pond and it's vicinity. Subsequently as shown and pointed out by accused Babul Mia (since deceased) and another confessing accused Piyas, the Investigating Officer P.W.I has recovered a rod for breaking grill and two daos from those places and the pond and seized the same by preparing seizure list in opresence of the witnesses and exhibited those as material Exts. Recovery of such articles by the Investigating Officer pointed out by the confessing accused is admissible in evidence under Section 27 of the Evidence Act.<em>The State -Vs.- Md. Sirajul Islam and others 1 ALR(2012) (HCD)185.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.5pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 30</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 8.4pt 0.7pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 30 of the Evidence Act enjoins that when more person than one are being tried jointly for the same offence and a confession made by one of such persons affecting himself and some other of such persons is proved, the Court may take into consideration such confession as against such persons as well as against the person who makes such confession.<em>The State -Vs.- Md. Sirajul Islam and others 1 ALR(2012) (HCD) 185.</em></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0.25pt 0.7pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 30 - Confessional statement against co-accused.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.45pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It is well settled that the confession of an accused is not a substantive piece of evidence against co-accused who did not confess and such evidence alone without any substantive corroborative evidence cannot form basis of conviction of co-accused. <em>Md. Kamal and others -Vs.- The State 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 1.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 9.85pt 1.2pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 30 - Confessional statement corroborated by the evidence of the eye witness.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.45pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The judicial confession of the condemned-appellant Masum stands corroborated by the evidence of the eye­witnesses to the occurrence. In other words, the judicial confession of Masum has been corroborated by the ocular evidence on record in material particulars. This being the position, there can be no hesitation in holding that the confessional statement of Masum is true as well as voluntary. <em>Masumur Rahman -Vs.- TheState 3 ALR(2014)(1) 312.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.7pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Confessional statement: Section 30</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.7pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The confessional statement made by condemned prisoner itself without being corroborated by other evidence cannot be considered as a piece of evidence as against non confessing accused.<em>The State-Vs.-Alam @ Md. Alam and others 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 517.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.25pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 45</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.1in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It appears that there was a deep love between the convict and victim as a result of which they got married and lived as husband and wife. It is a case of elopement and not abduction. The doctor did not find any recent sign of forcible sexual intercourse. So, she was the consenting party to the intercourse. The Kabinama shows that the age of the victim was 18 years and the oral evidence of the victim corroborates the same but the medical report shows that she was 13 to 14 years. The opinion of the doctor as to the age of the victim is not authenticated because as per Modi's Medical Jurisprudence in ascertaining the age of any person teeth is an important factor. In the present case the doctor has not taken into consideration the teeth in determining the same. The appearl is allowed setting aside the impugned judgment and order.<em> Mehedi Hasan alias Rasel-Vs-The State 1 ALR(2012) (HCD) 51.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.25pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 67 and 68</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.1in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The prosecution did not produce the scribe and the witnesses. No explanation has been given by the prosecution for withholding the scribe of exhibit (Ka), which is the sheet anchor of the case to prove the charges. The compromise petition has been reproduced in the judgment of the High Court Division and on perusal of the same, we find nothing therein that the accused persons have admitted their involvement in the incident. Therefore, this compromise petition has not improved the prosecution case in any manner. Thus the prosecution has miserably failed to prove the charges against the appellants by adducing legal evidence to connect them in the incident. The Tribunal as well as the High Court Divison has totally overlooked this aspect of the matter and convicted the appellants on hypothesis. (Per S.K. Sinha, J minority view). <em>Sree Rabindra Nath Roy @ Rabindra and another -Vs- The State 1 ALR (AD) 189</em></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.3pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section- 102 — Burden of proof lies on the prosecution but under special circumstances it shifts on the accused.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 0.1in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Since the victim wife was murdered while being under the custody of the accused husband and his behaviors following the murder are abnormal, the accused is to explain as to how the victim met with her death. In the absence of any plausible explanation coming from the side of the accused husband, It is to be found that none other than the accused husband is responsible for causing the death of the victim.<em>The State -Vs.- Shahinur Islam 3 ALR(2014)(1) 185.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 105</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.3pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The occurrence took place on 02-09-2001. P.Ws. 3, 4 were examined by the I.O. on 15-12-2001 and 17-11-2001 respectively, both P.Ws. 6-7 were examined by the I.O. on 30-11-2001 and P.W. 11 was examined after 3/4 months from the occurrence So inordinate delay in examining the important prosecution witnesses cast a serious doubt as to the truth of the prosecution case and in the circumstances their evidence cannot be relied on and are to be left out of consideration. In view of the settled principle of law the evidence of P.Ws. 3, 4, 6, 7 and 11 should not be relied on and the same are to be left out of consideration.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.3pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 106 read with Penal Code <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>(</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; font-variant: small-caps; letter-spacing: 1.0pt;">xlv </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">of 1860) </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 302-Conviction of an accused can be based on circumstantial evidence alone.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Appellate Division held that under the provisions of section 106 of the Evidence Act the husband has a special duty to explain what happened to his wife in the space of time when he was last seen with her and the time when her dead body was discovered since the victim was in his custody. It is the husband who is deemed to have special knowledge about the whereabouts of his wife and what happened to her in that interim period. The burden of proof is squarely on thehusband to prove how his wife met her death. <em>Shafiqul Islam @ Shafi-Vs.-The State 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)261.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section <span style="letter-spacing: -1.5pt;">114 ( g)</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Index prepared by subsequent I.O. P.W. 19 but surprisingly S.I. Luthfor Rahman was withheld by the prosecution without any explanation. Moreover most vital witnesses namely Abdur Rouf, Kalam, Shimul were not examined by the prosecution. From the evidence on record if appears that Nurul Islam Bachchu was survived by his wife, and two children, host of relatives and well-wishers but the prosecution failed to examine any of them without any proper explanation. So, the legal presumption would be had they been examined, they would not have supported the prosecution case.<em>The State -Vs- Pannu &amp; others 1 ALR(2012) (HCD) 87</em><strong><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">           </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section <span style="letter-spacing: -1.5pt;">114(g) </span>- non-examination of vital witness and statement of chance witness.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Non-examination of vital witness the presumption value will go against the prosecution case as per the provision of section 114(g) of the Evidence Act. That is to say if vital witness was examined then he would not supported the prosecution case. Thus after considering the evidence conduct and manner of P. W. <strong>2 </strong>who being a passerby can be treated him as a chance witness he adduced as a evidence of the case for the purpose of the prosecution<em> Md. Shahjahan Ali -Vs.- The State 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 245).</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section <span style="letter-spacing: -1.5pt;">114 (g) </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- Evidentiary value of the deposition of police personnel. - There is no reason to disbelieve the P.W's 1-4 only because they are police personnel when there is no contradiction or discrepancy rather consistency in their deposition.<em>Jahangir A lam -Vs.- The State 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 152</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.5pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 114 (g)-Adverse presumption</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In the face of the case made out in the FIR it is natural that people of the surroundings of the place of occurrence are most likely to come to the scene of the occurrence following the commission of murder of victim Nazrul Islam @ Naju and they could be the best witnesses of the case but the prosecution has withheld these material witnesses without any plausible explanation. Adverse presumption against the prosecutor, in the facts of the case, must be drawn, holding that had these natural and material witnesses been examined in the case, they would not support the prosecution case. <em>Ansar All Mallik -Vs.- The State 3 ALR(2014)(1) 294.<br/></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.5pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 114(g)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">As for the present case, it appears that neither the seizure list witnesses nor the local witnesses were examined by the prosecution. In the context of the fact of cited case, relating to corroboration appears to be distinguishable from the present case. Under the circumstances there is no hesitation in holding that the prosecution has totally failed to prove the recovery of the arms and bullet from the exclusive control and possession of the petitioner. It appears that non-examination of important witnesses creates presumption under section 114(g) of the Evidence Act and raises doubt about the prosecution case and benefit of doubt would always go in favour of the accused petitioner. The prosecution has miserably failed to prove recovery of arms and bullet from the exclusive control and possession of the petitioner by adducing reliable and independent evidence before the Tribunal. The impugned judgment and order is quashed. <em>@ Galcuta Hani/and Hanif.-Vs-The State 1 ALR (HCD)109</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 114 (g) </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- Evidentiary value of the deposition of police personnel. - There is no reason to disbelieve the P.W's 1-4 only because they are police personnel when there is no contradiction or discrepancy rather consistency in their deposition<em> Jahangir Alam -Vs.- The State 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 152</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 134 </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- It is a cardinal principle of law that the evidence of prosecutix generally carried much value. Even on the basis of solitary satisfactory testimony of the prosecutix can be form the basis of conviction if the said testimony of such witness is found to be entirely reliable and believable as well as trustworthy in the strong of section 134 of the Evidence Act. But in the instant case the testimony of the victim as discussed above. In where we find that admittedly the victim was divorced within 06 months of their marriage by her earlier husband. She filed petition of complaint before the court after 14 days in where she got opportunity to lodge F.I.R. or petition of complaint at the earliest point of time. So the petition of complaint of the victim was not free from subsequent embellishment. Moreover the victim was not examined by the doctor to determine her allegation of rape. The cause of action arose to file the petition of complaint due to refusal by the appellant to marry the victim not for committing rape. There is no other corroborative independent witness in support of P.W.I. <em>Md. Shahjahan All -Vs.- The State 5 ALR(HCD)2015(1) 245</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 145</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Appellate Division held that defence, by cross-examining the witnesses, could not make their testimonies as to the inflicting of blow by Shah Alam with ram dao on the deceased shaky. The defence did not even try to point out any contradiction in their testimonies within the meaning of section 145 of the Evidence Act by cross-examining the Investigation Officer on the question of inflicting ram dao blow by Shah Alam <em>the High Court Division </em>also failed to consider that the injury caused by Shah Alam upon the deceased with ram dao was clearly borne out from the post­mortem report. Therefore, Appellate Division found that accused Shah Alam committed an offence under section 307 of the Penal Code and he is liable to be punished accordingly. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span><strong>Section 145 and 157</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In a criminal case it is significant that the prosecution must prove the case beyond all reasonable doubt particularly the place of occurrence. P.Ws. 2, 3, 4, 7, 11 categorically stated that the deceased Nurul Islam Bachchu was chased by the accused from Kalam's house towards Abdul Roufs house, where he was shot dead. But P.W. 6 stated that he was chased from Jail road then to Kalam's house, lastly to the Roufs house. It is the definite case of the prosecution according to P.W. 1 that he was chased from Muftibari to Hasanfoez Lane, then near to the house of Rouf. Therefore, on an assessment of the evidence of aforesaid alleged eye witnesses, we find that the presence of those witnesses at the place of occurrence or about the time is doubtful from their testimony that either P.W.6 or P.Ws. 2-4, 7, 11 or F.I.R. or the evidence of P.W. 1 be believed or that none of them be believed. On the face of these inconsistencies it is difficult to rely on their testimony. <em>The State-Vs-<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Pannu &amp; others 1 ALR(2012) (HCD) 87.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 154-FIR</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Information disclosing a cognizable offence, which is first in point of time is not always the FIR of a case when an information disclosing a cognizable offence is first in point of time is vitiated by fraud aiming at frustrating the course of justice, such an information cannot be treated as the FIR of the case. In such a case, a subsequent authentic information shall be treated as the FIR of the case.<em>The State -Vs- Md. Zahid Hossain Jewel 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 219</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">— <strong>155 Weight to be attached to the testimony of a witness.</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The credit to be given to the evidence of a witness is a matter not regulated by rule of procedure but it depends on a large number of considerations such as natural probality, disinterestedness, integrity, veracity and consistency, with other evidence.<em> Lai Mohammad Vs State.-3 ALR(2014)(1) 87.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.9pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 164 -- Confessional statement –Value of a retracted confession.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">A confession duly recorded by a Magistrate, whether subsequently retracted or not, when found to be true and voluntary and is not the product of torture and intimidation, such a confession can safely be the basis of conviction. In the absence of any special reason, the retraction of a confession is of no benefit for the confessing accused. <em>The State -Vs- Md. Zahid Hossain Jewel 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 219.</em></span></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-fareast-theme-font: minor-fareast; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-language: BN;">Chance Witness A chance witness is one who claims to be present at the place of the occurrence at a time when he is not normally expected to be there. The evidence of a chance witness is a weak type of evidence and is not considered worthy in coming to a decision in a Criminal Case. <em>Jharna Begum - VS- The State 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 43.</em></span></p></div></div>

Name="Light Grid Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="63" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Shading 1 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="64" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Shading 2 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="65" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium List 1 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="66" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium List 2 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="67" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 1 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="68" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 2 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="69" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 3 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="70" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="21" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" QFormat="true" Name="Intense Emphasis"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="31" SemiHidden="false"
