<w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="39" QFormat="true" Name="TOC Heading"/> </w:LatentStyles></xml><![endif]--><!-- [if gte mso 10]><style> /* Style Definitions */ table.MsoNormalTable	{mso-style-name:"Table Normal";	mso-tstyle-rowband-size:0;	mso-tstyle-colband-size:0;	mso-style-noshow:yes;	mso-style-priority:99;	mso-style-qformat:yes;	mso-style-parent:"";	mso-padding-alt:0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;	mso-para-margin-top:0in;	mso-para-margin-right:0in;	mso-para-margin-bottom:10.0pt;	mso-para-margin-left:0in;	line-height:115%;	mso-pagination:widow-orphan;	font-size:11.0pt;	mso-bidi-font-size:14.0pt;	font-family:"Calibri","sans-serif";	mso-ascii-font-family:Calibri;	mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;	mso-hansi-font-family:Calibri;	mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;}</style><![endif]--></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 9.6pt 0.25pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">                                      Explosive Substances Act </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">(VI of 1908)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 3 - Explosion of a nature likely to endanger life or to cause serious injury.</span></strong></p><p class="Style4" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It is crystal clear that accused Masum unlawfully or maliciously caused by an explosive substance an explosion of a nature likely to endanger life or to cause serious injury to person or property and because of the bomb explosion, many people were injured and one Mozibul Haque sustained a grievous splinter injury on his person resulting in his death. This being the position, it leaves no room for doubt that accused Masum committed the offence punishable under Section 3 of the Explosive Substances Act. <em>Masumur Rahman - Vs. - The State 3 ALR(2014)(1) 312</em></span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><br/></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 4</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The prosecution proved the date, time, place and manner and as well as proved the occurrence and well established the case. The learned Judge of the Tribunal found the accused guilty and sentenced him legally. The entire body of the evidence has successfully proved against the accused appellant. The learned Judge of the Tribunal has rightly convicted and sentenced the accused appellant Rashid Sarder legally and with cogent ground. In the result, the jail appeal is stand dismissed. <em>Rashid Sarder - Vs. The State 6 ALR - 2015(2)120.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Extra- judicial confession to be the basis of conviction needs corroboration by independent and disinterested witness.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Admittedly the disputed sarees were not recovered from the possession of the accused petitioner but these were recovered from the roof-top the bus.The assertion of the prosecution that the accused petitioner claimed the sarees as his own after these were seized by the police, invariably warranting criminal liability, is hardly a relievable story .In the absence of any corroboration to the evidence of the members of the recovery party, the impugned order of conviction cannot be sustained. <em>Motahar Hossain - VS- The State 2 ALR(2013)(HCD) 49.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.05pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Further investigation or re-investigation</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The police has filed charge sheet finding the allegation prima facie proved. It may be mentioned here that there is no bar in any law for further investigation or re­investigation of any case and for submission of charge sheet where, earlier, the police filed final report finding no evidence. In the present case since police, on investigation, found the allegation prima facie proved there is no bar in submission of charge sheet and also in accepting the same by the Court.<em>Ms. Ok Kyung Oh-Vs.-Mr. Bo-Sun Park and another 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)143.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Forging the signature</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Appellate Division found that in the facts and circumstances of the present case the High Court Division was wrong in holding the view that since the allegations in the case in question is identical with one of the allegations in Motijheel Police Station Case No. 72 dated 20.03.2005 this present case cannot be allowed to proceed ignoring the broad facts that the said Motijheel Police Station Case No. 72 dated 20.03.2005 has already ended with the submission of final report by the police and the accused-respondent was not at all prosecuted in that Motijheel Police Station Case No. 72 dated 20.03.2005 and was not either convicted or acquitted. The Appellate Division found no bar in proceeding with the present case on the allegations of creating a false resignation letter forging the signature of the appellant thereon and submission of the same to the Registrar of the Joint Stock. Companies and Fims. Hence, this appeal be allowed on contest. <em>Ms. Ok Kyung Oh-Vs.-Mr. Bo-Sun Park and another 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)143</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.9pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Facts and circumstances incompatible with the innocence of the accused invariably lead to the inference of his guilt.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When the facts and circumstances of the case are found totally incompatible with the innocence of the accused and there can be no reasonable hypothesis other than his guilt, conviction can be safely awarded to the accused.<em>The State - Vs.- Monir Hossain alias Monir 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 373.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 11.5pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Extenuating circumstances</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Since a considerable period has been spent in the death cell and the sword of death has been hanging on the neck of the petitioner, who suffered from mental agony of death for the long period which may be considered as extenuating circumstances for commuting the sentence of death penalty to that of imprisonment for life. <em>Monirul Islam @ Manir-Vs.- The State. 4 ALR (AD) 2014 (2) 156</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; tab-stops: right 212.65pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Judicial decrees may not change the heart, but they can restrain the heartless.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; tab-stops: right 212.9pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Morality cannot be legislated, but behavior can be regulated. Judicial decrees may not change the heart, but they can restrain the heartless. <em>Sukur Mahmood and others. -Vs.-The State. 4 ALR (AD) 2014 (2) 81</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.9pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Failure to enhiit the 'falah' as material exhibit cannot make prosecution case doubtful.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; tab-stops: right 212.9pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Soon after the occurrence, accused petitioner who was carrying the 'falah' fled away from the place of occurrence with the 'falah' and as such, the failure of the prosecution in making the 'falah' as material exhibit cannot make its case doubtful.<em> Shahjahan Khalifa - Vs.- The State 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 55.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Fugitive from justice cannot seek justice without surrounding before a Court of law.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; tab-stops: right 212.9pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It is a settled principle of law that a fugitive from justice cannot get the protection of law. The accused did not surrender to the trial court after his bail was cancelled and warrant of arrest issued. He moved the High Court Division without surrendering there, and, therefore, the revisional petition ought not to have been entertained nor the Rule issued. The swearing of the affidavit was illegal. The revisional petition filed before the High Court Division shows that the respondent did not appear before the Commissioner of Affidavits and the cause title of the petition does not state that the petitioner was in custody, or was on bail, or appeared in person before the High Court Division. The issuance of the Rule was illegal as was the grant of bail, which was cancelled by the Appellate Division and warrant of arrest was directed to be issued. <em>The State- - Vs.- Dr. Fazlur Rahman 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 136.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Fundamental right of foreign prisoners</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Our considered view is that the failure of the Government to take steps in this matter is violation of fundamental right of foreign prisoners which have been guaranteed in Articles 31 and 32 of the Constitution. <em>Rana Singha.-Vs State.- 3 ALR(2014)(1) 208.</em></span></p></div></div>

class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.45pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                       </span>General Clauses Act [X of 1897]</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 26 - The offender cannot be punished twice for the same offence.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Where an act or omission constitutes an offence under two or more enactments, then the offender shall be liable to be prosecuted and punished under either or any of those enactments, but shall not be liable to be punished twice for the same offence. But the offence punishable under Section 302 of the Penal Code and the offence punishable under Section 3 of the Explosive Substances Act are not one and the same; rather they are distinct and separate offences. Askk they are distinct and separate offences. In the facts of the case of Section 26 of the General Clauses Act cannot be invoked. <em>Masumur Rahman - Vs.- The State 3 ALR(2014)(1) 312.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.4pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Grounds of detention must not be vague, indefinite, unspecific and omnibus.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In the grounds of detention the detenu was described as a narcotics trader, illegal arms-holder, collector of illegal toll , extortionist and a terrorist but the grounds did not disclose any fact and material showing that he was an illegal arms-holder, toll collector and an extortionist. These grounds of detention were evidently quite vague and indefinite and did not give sufficient materials to the detenu enabling him to make an effective representation to the detaining authority against his order of detention. In such view of the matter , the initial order of detention passed against the detenu must be held illegal. Consequently, the subsequent order of the Government extending the detention for a further period of 90 days is equally illegal and unauthorized. <em>Md. Shafiqul Islam -Vs.- The state 2 ALR(2013)(HCD) 196.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.4pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The hostile witnesses can not be discarded</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The hostile evidence of P.W.I5, are supported by the evidence of P.Ws. 16 and 18 along with the statement of the inquest report Exhibit-7 can not be discarded only because which are favourable to the accused appellant.<em>The State. -Vs.- Abdul Khalek 6 ALR - 2015(2)54.</em></span></p></div></div>

table.MsoNormalTable	{mso-style-name:"Table Normal";	mso-tstyle-rowband-size:0;	mso-tstyle-colband-size:0;	mso-style-noshow:yes;	mso-style-priority:99;	mso-style-qformat:yes;	mso-style-parent:"";	mso-padding-alt:0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;	mso-para-margin-top:0in;	mso-para-margin-right:0in;	mso-para-margin-bottom:10.0pt;	mso-para-margin-left:0in;	line-height:115%;	mso-pagination:widow-orphan;	font-size:11.0pt;	mso-bidi-font-size:14.0pt;	font-family:"Calibri","sans-serif";	mso-ascii-font-family:Calibri;	mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;	mso-hansi-font-family:Calibri;	mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;}</style><![endif]--></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.45pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                       </span>General Clauses Act [X of 1897]</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 26 - The offender cannot be punished twice for the same offence.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Where an act or omission constitutes an offence under two or more enactments, then the offender shall be liable to be prosecuted and punished under either or any of those enactments, but shall not be liable to be punished twice for the same offence. But the offence punishable under Section 302 of the Penal Code and the offence punishable under Section 3 of the Explosive Substances Act are not one and the same; rather they are distinct and separate offences. Askk they are distinct and separate offences. In the facts of the case of Section 26 of the General Clauses Act cannot be invoked. <em>Masumur Rahman - Vs.- The State 3 ALR(2014)(1) 312.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.4pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Grounds of detention must not be vague, indefinite, unspecific and omnibus.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In the grounds of detention the detenu was described as a narcotics trader, illegal arms-holder, collector of illegal toll , extortionist and a terrorist but the grounds did not disclose any fact and material showing that he was an illegal arms-holder, toll collector and an extortionist. These grounds of detention were evidently quite vague and indefinite and did not give sufficient materials to the detenu enabling him to make an effective representation to the detaining authority against his order of detention. In such view of the matter , the initial order of detention passed against the detenu must be held illegal. Consequently, the subsequent order of the Government extending the detention for a further period of 90 days is equally illegal and unauthorized. <em>Md. Shafiqul Islam -Vs.- The state 2 ALR(2013)(HCD) 196.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.4pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The hostile witnesses can not be discarded</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The hostile evidence of P.W.I5, are supported by the evidence of P.Ws. 16 and 18 along with the statement of the inquest report Exhibit-7 can not be discarded only because which are favourable to the accused appellant.<em>The State. -Vs.- Abdul Khalek 6 ALR - 2015(2)54.</em></span></p></div></div>

table.MsoNormalTable	{mso-style-name:"Table Normal";	mso-tstyle-rowband-size:0;	mso-tstyle-colband-size:0;	mso-style-noshow:yes;	mso-style-priority:99;	mso-style-qformat:yes;	mso-style-parent:"";	mso-padding-alt:0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;	mso-para-margin-top:0in;	mso-para-margin-right:0in;	mso-para-margin-bottom:10.0pt;	mso-para-margin-left:0in;	line-height:115%;	mso-pagination:widow-orphan;	font-size:11.0pt;	mso-bidi-font-size:14.0pt;	font-family:"Calibri","sans-serif";	mso-ascii-font-family:Calibri;	mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;	mso-hansi-font-family:Calibri;	mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;}</style><![endif]--></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 90.7pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.15pt 0in .0001pt 11.75pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">        </span>International Crimes Tribunals Act</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 5.75pt .95pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                                      </span>[XIX of 1973]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 3 (2) </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- The Appellate Division does not find any illegality in their Appellate judgment. Hence the Review petition is dismissed The Appellate Division held that petitioner's ruthless Badr Bahini being instigated, suggested, provoked and incited by the petitioner had kidnapped and killed the intellectuals which was cold blooded savagery. Such barbaric gruesome brutal crimes which are comparable with the Hitler's Gas Chamber Genocide or Jalilianbag massacre. Does Islam permit killing of those unarmed people? While awarding the sentence, the Court must take into consideration the unbearable pains, tears rolling down the cheeks and sufferings of the widows and children of the victims who cried for getting justice for about 43 years. The barbaric gruesome and heinous crimes which under the petitioner's leadership his Badr Bahini committed is a revolt against the humanity. As leader of Badr Bahini the petitioner can not escape from the liability. It is the duty of the court to impose proper punishment depending upon the criminality and proportionate to the gravity of the offence. The Appellate Division does not find any wrong in the ultimate conclusion of the Tribunal which has been affirmed by the Appellate judgment. The Appellate Division' does not find any illegality in their <strong><em><span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></em></strong>judgment. Hence the Review petition is dismissed.<em>Ali Ahsan Muhammad Mujahid-Vs.-The Chief, Prosecutor, International Crimes Tribunal Dhaka,Bangladesh 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)154.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .95pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Inquest Report is the best evidence</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Since the name of the accused appellant was not disclosed neither by P.W.I nor by P.W.I5 who were the eye witnesses of the occurrence at the time of inquest of the dead body by the P.W.I6 the investigating officer. Therefore the name of the accused appellant was omitted in the body of the inquest report. The delay of 8 hours in lodging the F.I.R. with Police station also remained unexplained. The prosecution witnesses are the local chairman and his men who after arrived at the place of occurrence on the same date after sun set then the informant lodged the F.I.R. by mentioning the name of the accused appellant for the first time suddenly. While the inimical to the accused appellant with the local chairman P.W.7 is admitted by the men of the local Chairman P.Ws. 4, 6, 8 and 9 including the conduct of the Chairman P.W.7 himself. The High Court Division find that the inquest report exhibit No. 7 of the dead body of the victim and its statement of the investigating officer P.W.I6 is the direct or primary evidence in the eye of law. Thus the same is the best evidence in the case and it is not proved as to be suspected and unreliable perfunctory or dishonest otherwise.<em>The State. - Vs.- Abdul Khalek 6 ALR - 2015(2)54</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .95pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Judicial confessions</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The High Court Division does do not find any explanation from the side of the defence as to the safe departure of the victim Azim Uddin from the company of the accused Uzzal and Shamim after he was called away at 7:00 P.M. on 30.09.2004. It is admitted that the dead body of the victim was recovered from the sugarcane field on the following day (01.10.2004). The non-furnishing of any explanation, let alone the question of any reasonable explanation, as to the safe departure of the victim Azim from the company of the accused Uzzal and Shamim is indicative of their guilt corroborating their judicial confessions made to the Magistrate (P.W. 13). <em>Md. Uzzal Hossain and others -Vs-The State 6 ALR - 2015(2)269.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Leniency in awarding punishment when not justified.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 7.7pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When the offence is not only heinous in nature but also shockingly cruel and pre­meditated, the offender is apt to be regarded as enemy of the society. In such a case, no leniency in the matter of sentence is called for. <em>Shahid Ullah -Vs.- The State 3 ALR(2014)(1)(AD) 192.</em></span></p></div></div>

<w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="39" QFormat="true" Name="TOC Heading"/> </w:LatentStyles></xml><![endif]--><!-- [if gte mso 10]><style> /* Style Definitions */ table.MsoNormalTable	{mso-style-name:"Table Normal";	mso-tstyle-rowband-size:0;	mso-tstyle-colband-size:0;	mso-style-noshow:yes;	mso-style-priority:99;	mso-style-qformat:yes;	mso-style-parent:"";	mso-padding-alt:0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;	mso-para-margin-top:0in;	mso-para-margin-right:0in;	mso-para-margin-bottom:10.0pt;	mso-para-margin-left:0in;	line-height:115%;	mso-pagination:widow-orphan;	font-size:11.0pt;	mso-bidi-font-size:14.0pt;	font-family:"Calibri","sans-serif";	mso-ascii-font-family:Calibri;	mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;	mso-hansi-font-family:Calibri;	mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;}</style><![endif]--></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">                                                                 Martial Law</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">There is no such law in Bangladesh as Martial Law and there is no such Authority as Martial Law Authority as such and if any person declares martial law, he will be liable for high treason against the Republic. Obedience to superior orders is no defence. <em>M. Anwar Hossain -Vs.- Government of Bangladesh 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 253.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The taking over of powers of the Government of the People's Republic of Bangladesh with effect form the morning of 15th August, 1975 by Khandakar Mustak Ahmed an usurper, placing Bangladesh under martial law and his assumption of office of the President of Bangladesh, were in clear violation of the Constitution, as such, illegal, without lawful authority. <em>M. Anwar Hossain -Vs.- Government of Bangladesh 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 253</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 9.6pt 2.65pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In view of the sequence of events and the evidence on record it is evidently clear that the requirements of a "fair trial" were conspicuously missing in the case. The so-called regulation that engendered the so-called tribunal did not lay down the above- cited requirements. The trial was held in camera and as such it lacked public character. An oath of secrecy thrust upon all who took part in the trial process further devastated its acceptability and rendered the purported trial a clandestine exercise. <em>M. Anwar Hossain -Vs.- Government of Bangladesh 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 253.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 9.6pt 2.65pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Death sentence passed on Col. Taher was by far the most dreadful factor that totally and, indeed, conspicuously, infested the whole scenario with squalid stink because of the legislative schemes, and even the so-called Martial Law Regulations did not empowers the so-called Tribunal to pass death sentence on the date the impugned trial commenced. The purported death sentence was "thus" imposed refluxing sheer gun power in whimsical and ludicrous defiance of those laws that were promulgated by the military usurpers.<em>M. Anwar Hossain -Vs.- Government of Bangladesh 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 253</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 9.85pt .7pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The sentence of death imposed on Col. Taher and the consequent execution is nothing but a cold-blooded murder on three counts: first, the execution being corried out without any legal sanction is murder, secondly it was a clear murder because even on the date of commencement of the so-called trial, none of the charges brought against the accused prescribed death sentence and finally, the death sentence was pre­determined by General Ziaur Rahaman well before the Special Martial Law Tribunal was constituted, at a meeting of the formation commanders. Irrespective of the question of the legal status of the so-called Tribunal, the events that prevailed within the canopy of the Dhaka Central Jail, can by no means, be termed as a judicially recognized criminal trial. It cannot even be termed as a drama of a criminal trial- It was a hoax in the protext of a judicial trial. It is thus clear that the excution of Col. Taher Bir-Uttom, was a cold-blooded marder engineered by General Ziaur Rahman. <em>M. Anwar Hossain -Vs.- Government of Bangladesh 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 253</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The dastardly killing of Col. Taher, Bir-Uttam deprived Bangladesh of the service of a valiant freedom fighter whose contribution to our liberation War can hardly be exaggerated. This loathsome event will represent a blotted era in our history.<em>M. Anwar Hossain -Vs.- Government of Bangladesh 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 253</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In view of the findings of the Hon'ble Court an obligation is cast upon the authorities to wipe out the names of all the accused and the spouses of petitioner Nos. 2 and 3 of Writ Petition No.7236/10 from the criminal records that came into being in consequence of the illegal conviction and to project them with unblemished image, while the execution of Col. Taher Bir-Uttam must be recorded as a clear cut extra-judicial murder. Order dismissing Major Ziauddin, Corporal Shamsul Hauque, Habilder Abdul Hai Mazumder (Writ Petition No. 1048/11) and Abdul Majid(Writ Petition No. 1059/11) must be reversed and they shall be deemed to be in service till their normal retirement age.<em> M. Anwar Hossain -Vs.- Government of Bangladesh 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 253.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Regard being had to the fact that Major Ziauddin, is a Freedom Fighter of national repute, with his commendable achievement during his cadetship, it is reasonable to believe that he would have risen at least to the rank of a Brigadier General had he not been illegally dismissed.<em>M. Anwar Hossain -Vs.- Government of Bangladesh 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 253.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 9.1pt 2.15pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Since promotion of the officer of the armed forces is not automatic, the authority is directed to pay Major Ziauddin the money he would have received as a Major along with all service benefits had he not been illegally dismissed from service till his normal retirement. <em>The same shall apply to Corporal Shamsul Hauque, Habilder Abdul Hai Mazumder, and Md. Abdul Majid. M. Anwar Hossain -Vs.- Government of Bangladesh 2 ALR (2013) (HCD) 253.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It will be open to the authority to decorate Major Ziauddin with the superior rank and honour in recognition of his most brilliant contribution to our War of Liberation.<em>M. Anwar Hossain -Vs.- Government of Bangladesh 2 ALR (2013) (HCD) 253.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 27.35pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></em></p></div></div>

UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Grid Accent 6"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="19" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" QFormat="true" Name="Subtle Emphasis"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="21" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" QFormat="true" Name="Intense Emphasis"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="31" SemiHidden="false" <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="33" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" QFormat="true" Name="Book Title"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="37" Name="Bibliography"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="39" QFormat="true" Name="TOC Heading"/> </w:LatentStyles></xml><![endif]--><!-- [if gte mso 10]><style> /* Style Definitions */ table.MsoNormalTable	{mso-style-name:"Table Normal";	mso-tstyle-rowband-size:0;	mso-tstyle-colband-size:0;	mso-style-noshow:yes;	mso-style-priority:99;	mso-style-qformat:yes;	mso-style-parent:"";	mso-padding-alt:0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;	mso-para-margin-top:0in;	mso-para-margin-right:0in;	mso-para-margin-bottom:10.0pt;	mso-para-margin-left:0in;	line-height:115%;	mso-pagination:widow-orphan;	font-size:11.0pt;	mso-bidi-font-size:14.0pt;	font-family:"Angsana New","serif";	mso-hansi-font-family:Calibri;	mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;	mso-bidi-language:BN;}</style><![endif]--></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.9pt; text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Narcotics Control Act</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: .25pt; text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">[XX of 1990]</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .25pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 19, Table 1(b)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The quantity of heroine was not at all ascertained. Without ascertaining the quantity of heroine the conviction under Section 19, Table 1(b) is illegal and not sustainable. <em>Sahidur Rahman -Vs.- The State 3 ALR(2014)(1)172.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .5pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections - 31, 39 and 44</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 31 of the Act has made the offence committed under this Act cognizable. Section 39(i) of the Act has given power of an Officer—in charge of a Police Station to the Directorate to investigate into an offence under this Act. Sub-section (2) of section 39 empowers the Government to confer power of an Officer-in-charge of a Police Station to an officer subordinate to the Director General of the Narcotics Directorate by a gazette notification to investigate into any offence under this Act. It is thus evident that the power of the Director General of the Narcotics Directorate is not in derogation of the power of the Officer-in-charge of the concerned Police Station. Under section 5(2) of the Code of Criminal Procedure. Section 44—Section 44 of the Act shows that on a written request by the Director General of the Directorate of Narcotics, the investigating agency may hand over charge of investigation of a case. It is thus clear that besides the Director General of the Directorate of Narcotics an officer subordinate to him specially empowered by the Government, investigation of an offence under this Act may also be done by any designated member of the law enforcing agency competent to investigate the case. The power of the Director General of the Directorate of Narcotics to investigate a case under this Act is neither exclusive nor absolute. <em>The State-Vs.- Amin Huda 2 ALR (2013)(AD) 177.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 44</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> of the Act shows that on a written request by the Director General of the Directorate of Narcotics, the investigating agency may hand over charge of investigation of a case. It is thus clear that besides the Director General of the Directorate of Narcotics an officer subordinate to him specially empowered by the Government, investigation of an offence under this Act may also be done by any designated member of the law enforcing agency competent to investigate the case. The power of the Director General of the Directorate of Narcotics to investigate a case under this Act is neither exclusive nor absolute. <em>The State-Vs.- Am in Huda 2 ALR (2013)(AD) 177.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">No moral conviction is contemplated in law.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The prosecution can succeed in securing conviction of the accused only on satisfactory legal evidence. Suspicion whatsoever high cannot be a substitute for legal evidence and cannot therefore take the place of legal evidence. In the instant case there is absolutely no legal evidence on record to prove the guilt of the accused persons and as such the impugned order of conviction of the condemned pensioners solely based on suspicion is not maintainable in law. Therefore, the impugned order of conviction being a moral conviction must be set aside. <em>The State -Vs.- Abdul Quiyum 2 ALR(2013)(HCD) 160 </em><strong>Natural presumption </strong>When the wife is murdered while in custody of her husband the natural presumption will be that her husband is responsible for her death. <em>The State -Vs.- Khorshed Pesker 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 100.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 5.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">No review lies except on ground of error apparent on the face of the record or miscarriage of justice.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Appellate Division held that the learned Counsel could not show any error in the decision in arriving at the conclusion that the plea of alibi has not been substituted or that the reasons assigned by the Appellate Division are contrary to the evidence on record or that there are error apparent on the face of the record. No review lies in this court except on ground of error apparent on the face of the record or miscarriage of justice. The basic philosophy inherent in it is the universal acceptance of human fallibility. The learned Counsel fails to point out any error which has been cropped up on analysis of the evidence on record. Since the learned Counsel did not argue on the merit of the 13 matter, and stresses upon the plea of alibi, which has been rejected on a full flagged hearing, at the late stage the petitioner has renewed the plea by producing a spurious document. Further, the learned Counsel having not argued on merit pointing any error in the impugned judgment, it is apparent that there is no error of law in the impugned judgment for the Appellate Division interference. The Appellate Division found no cogent ground to review our judgment. The review petition is accordingly dismissed. <em>Salauddin Qader Chowdhury -Vs.-Bangladesh  6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)133.</em></span></p><p> </p></div></div>
