inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Appellate Division held that-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 0in; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: .5in; margin: 7.7pt 1.2pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sub-sections (2) and (4) of section 6 of the Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 1995 and sub-sections (2) and (3) of section 34 of the Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Ain, 2000 and section 303 of the Penal code are declared ultravires the Constitution.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; text-indent: 0in; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: .5in; margin: 7.7pt .25pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Despite repeal of the Ain of 1995, the pending cases and pending appeals in respect of those offences shall be tried and heard in accordance with the provisions of the Ain of 1995, but the sentences prescribed in respect of similar nature of offences in the Ain of 2000 shall be applicable.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 7.7pt 0.25pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-indent: 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">There shall be no mandatory sentence of death in respect of an offence of murder committed by an offender who is under a sentence of life imprisonment.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; tab-stops: .5in; margin: 7.7pt .25pt .0001pt 0in;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Bangladesh Legal Aid and Services Trust (BLAST) and others-Vs.-Bangladesh. 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)01</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 17.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                       </span>Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain, 1995, </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 17.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                                </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">[XVIII of 1995]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 6 (1) and 14 - Reasonable doubt.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 9.35pt .7pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Appellate Division has observed that the story of rape itself gives rise to a grave suspicion implicating the accused, as such it will be fully within the domain of the appellate court to acquit the accused. Moreover, the reason of delay in lodging FIR even after the release of the victim from the clutch of the accused has not been properly described; so it is very difficult to consider the evidence of prosecutrix, as beyond any reasonable doubt which is the fundament requirement of conviction of an accused person.(Majority view) </span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The State- Vs. -Mostafizur Rahman and another 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)205.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.15in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                     </span>Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 1.2pt 0in 0.0001pt 79.45pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                              </span>[VIII of 2000]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 3 <br/></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.4pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Ain,2000, being a special law, has been enacted by the legislature with the intent and purpose to provide for stringent provisions for prevention of offences of oppression to women and children and to provide for adequate measures for effective elimination of the offences related thereto . Section 3 provides that the provisions of this Ain shall prevail notwithstanding anything contained in any other law for the time being in force. On a careful reading of the Ain it appears that the scheme of the legislation is initially for the complainant to lodge a complaint with any authorized police officer an authorized person and if he fails after making request in getting the complaint accepted or authorized person, then he may file a complaint accompanied by an affidavit before the tribunal whereupon the tribunal, having been satisfied, after examining the complainant, may direct "any Magistrate or any person" to enquire into the complaint and submit report within 7 working days. <em>Sirajul Islam </em>@ <em>A Suban-Vs.- The State and others 1 ALR(2012) (HCD) 162.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.4pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 5,6 and 30 - Penalty for trafficking women and children.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.4pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The High Court after considering the submissions made by the learned Advocates of both the parties and perusing the petition under section 561A of the Code of Criminal Procedure and petition of appeal and the Jail Appeal and also the judgment and order, it is clear that the prosecution adduced as many as 19 witnesses including the victims namely Most. Salma, Most. Jesmin, Most, Parveen, Most. Fatema , Most.Romesa Khatun, Most. Fatema and Most. Shefali Khatun who deposed in the court as P.Ws. and disclosed their agony after recovery when they were kept firstly in the house of Ahmed Ali then in the house of Mohammad Ali and thereafter in the house of Mohor Ali and lastly in the house of the convict-Nazrul which is situated within 1 and <strong><em><sup><span style="letter-spacing: -1.0pt;">l</span></sup><span style="letter-spacing: -1.0pt;">A </span></em></strong>kilometers from the border between India and Bangladesh. From the above circumstances there is no doubt that these women were collected and gathered by inducing to provide with a good jobs. The prosecution adduced sufficient evidence to show that they were kept near the border in order to traffic them to India in return of huge amount of money. Fortunately, the local people could realize the incidence and recovered the victim women from the area along with 4 convicts but some of the convicts could escape therefrom. In this regard it is clear that the offencesunder section 5,6 and section 30 of the A in have been committed by the convicts. <em>Md. Mohor AH -Vs.- The State, 3ALR(2014)(1)347</em></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 7.7pt 0in .0001pt 21.35pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjaton (Bishes Bidhan) Ain</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 7.7pt 0in .0001pt 21.35pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">[XVIII </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">of 1995]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 6(1) - Custody of the mother is certainly safer for minor victim than that of the jail.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In consideration of the allegation made in the FIR, the statement of the victim and the medical report the trial Court earlier released the victim to the custody of her mother, the present petitioner. There was no allegation of misuse of the custodial responsibility of the mother. The Public Prosecutor on his own initiative filed an application before the Trial Court praying for sending the minor victim to Jail custody and the prayer was allowed. The High Court Division, in the facts and circumstances of the case, held that the impugned order sending the minor victim to jail custody from the safe custody of her mother is highly unjust and untenable. The victim would remain in her mother's custody till the disposal of the case. <em>Mst. Rizia Khatoon, -Vs.-The State. 4 ALR 2014(2) 35</em>.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 7.7pt 0in .0001pt 21.35pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                          </span>Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                                  </span>[VIII of 2000]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 7</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                          </span>Evidence Act</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> [I of 1872]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 45</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.2pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It appears that there was a deep love between the convict and victim as a result of which they got married and lived as husband and wife. It is a case of elopement and not abduction. The doctor did not find any recent sign of forcible sexual intercourse. So, she was the consenting party to the intercourse. The Kabinama shows that the age of the victim was 18 years and the oral evidence of the victim corroborates the same but the medical report shows that she was 13 to 14 years. The opinion of the doctor as to the age of the victim is not authenticated because as per Modi's Medical Jurisprudence in ascertaining the age of any person teeth is an important factor. In the present case the doctor has not taken into consideration the teeth in determining the same. The appearl is allowed setting aside the impugned judgment and order. <em>Mehedi Hasan alias Rasel-Vs-The State 1 ALR(2012) (HCD) 51.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.2pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                           </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">               </span></span></em><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-0-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                                         </span>(VIII of 2000)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.2pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 7,9(1) and 30</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">-To ascertain the age of any person teeth is an important factor, the opinion of the doctor as to the age of the victim is not authenticated one. We should bear in mind that age is always depend upon the growth of the person who has been examined, a male or female of 18 years can be found as 15 or 16 years due to lack of his or her development of the body and again a male or female of 18 years can be found as 19 or 20 years and the reason is that his or her development and puberty was earlier. So, the opinion of the doctor as to the age of the victim is not authenticated one in our view because the way the victim should be examined has not been done. There is no opinion as to the teeth, because as per Modi's Medical Jurisprudence to ascertain the age of any person teeth is an important factor. 'Modi' has also observed 'the progressive increase in height and weight according to age varies so greatly in individuals that it cannot be depend upon in estimating age in medico legal cases.' The impugned judgment and order of conviction and sentence under section 7 of the Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Ain 2000 is here by set-aside. The convict appellant is acquitted from the charge leveled against him. <em>Mehedi Hasan alias Rasel - Vs.- The State 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 84.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 2.4pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 7 and 9(3)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .25pt 2.65pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The High Court Division absolute the Rule and acquitted the accused the state filed<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>leave<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>petition,<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the Appellate Division observed that the victim, as informant, lodged the First Information Report naming the accused respondent as one of the perpetrators involved in abducting and raping her. She maintained her story of abduction and rape in he deposition before the Court. The trial Court upon assessment of the evidence convicted and sentenced the respondent along with others, although the trial took place in the absence of all the accused persons, the case is remanded to the trial Court so far as it relates to accused respondent Robin with the direction to allow the accused to cross-examine the witnesses, if he so desires and to conclude the trial in accordance with law. The accused respondent Robin be enlarged on bail to the satisfaction of the trial Court till conclusion of the trial. <em>The State-Vs.-Robin. 4 ALR (AD) 2014 (2) 168.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .25pt 2.65pt .0001pt 0in;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .25pt 2.65pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 7, 9(1) and 30 </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- The victim declined to be examined medically she admitted in her cross-examination that she met and talked to the inmates of the house including a sister of the accused and her husband as well as other persons who visited the house. When she was taken to another village, she stated that people asked her questions. There is no mention that she complained to them about<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>her<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>abduction<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>or<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>rape. The informant alleged to have narrated the occurrence first of all to one Rokeya Begum, a neighbor who was not examined by the prosecution in the absence of any reason for not calling her as a witness a negative inference can drawn against the prosecution for not examining her. <em>The State -Vs.- Md. Palash 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 84</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 8.9pt 0in .0001pt 17.5pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                        </span>Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 8.9pt 0in .0001pt 17.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                             </span>[XVIII of 1995]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.45pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 8(1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .25pt 2.65pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Appellate Division observed that the High Court Division came to a finding that the petition of complaint was lodged on 30.11.1998 and that the FIR was lodged on 01.12.1998 and that while she was recovered from the brothel on 30.11.1998, police went to the brothel on 29.11.1998 on the basis of G. D. No. 1398 dated 30.11.1998 which was made for the security of the victim and that after recovery of the victim, the FIR was lodged. The High Court Division further found that P.W.I, the informant and P.W.2, the victim and P.Ws.4 and 5 deposed that the accused took the victim with a promise to give her job and without doing so they sold her to a brothel and that there was no contradiction in the evidence of the victim and that of her father, P.W.I. <em>Sukur Mahmood and others. -Vs.-The State. 4 ALR (AD) 2014 (2) 81.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 18.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                        </span>Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan (Bishesh Bidhan) Ain </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 18.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                          </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">[XVIII of 1995]</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 9 (Ga)/6(1)/14 Allegations after 14 days - Benefit of doubt</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Non discloser of the material allegation at the earliest opportunities and alleged subsequently after 14 days from the date of occurrence by the P.W. 1 also an element to cast a doubt of the prosecution case while there is no legal and reliable explanation under what circumstances the P. W. 1 informant did not disclose the material allegation neither before the police nor before the Magistrate while she was produced before them immediately after occurrence under Section 54 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. <em>Md. Shahjahan All - Vs.- The State 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 244.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 5.3pt .7pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                    </span>Nari-0-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                    </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">             </span>[VIII of 2000]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section- 9 read with clause(Uma) and (Ta) of section-2 of the said Ain.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Since a child under the age of sixteen is not in a position to give consent to sexual intercourse or sodomy, the sodomy committed by a man even on a consenting male-child will also come under the mischief of rape punishable under Section 9 (1) of the said Ain. Thus, the criminal proceeding in such cases must be instituted and proceeded against the perpetrator-man under the provisions of the said Ain. <em>Md. Abdus Samed -Vs- The State 3 ALR(2014)(1) 56.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 9(1)- DNA test.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The High Court Division asked for a DNA test report to ascertain that whether the accused appellant^ Md. Islam) is the biological father of the child (Milon) who is out come<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>co-habitation the accused appellant and victim( Mala Khaton), DNA Profiling Laboratory, reported that the accused-appellant is the father of the said child, under such circumstances the High Court Division dismissed the appeal and convict the appellant with sentence for life.<em>Md.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Islam<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>-Vs.- The State 3 ALR(2014)(1) 455.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 9.6pt 0in .0001pt 18.7pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                   </span>Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman (Bishes Bidhan) Ain</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 9.6pt 0in .0001pt 18.7pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                 </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">          </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">[VIII of 2000]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.9pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section ll(ka) - When the wife met with her death while she was in the custody of her husband it is he who is to explain how she met with her death.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">A person who caused death of his wife life out of sheer greed has no right to live in this world. He has committed cold blooded murder of a simple village girl just because her parents and she had failed to meet his illegal demands. In such a situation, the Tribunal has committed no illegality in passing the sentence of death. <em>The State -Vs.- Khorshed Pesker 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 100.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.05pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                      </span>Nari-0-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 5.75pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; font-variant: small-caps; letter-spacing: 1.0pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                          </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">            </span> [viii </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">of 2000]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 11 (Ka) - Cold blooded murder.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.8pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The High Court Division considered the evidence of the prosecution witnesses and found that they uniformly deposed that the convict accused had demanded dowry and subsequently due to non-fulfillment of the said demand, the deceased while in the custody of her husband was done to death by her husband convict accused. Considering the facts and circumstances of the case, the High Court held that the trial court has rightly awarded the sentence of death. Such a person who caused death of his wife out of sheer greed has no right to live in this world. He has committed cold blooded murder of a simple village girl just because her parents and she had failed to meet his illegal demands. In such a situation, the High Court Division is of the view that the Tribunal has committed no illegality in passing the sentence of death. <em>The State -Vs.- Oliar Rahman @ Olid. 4 ALR 2014(2) 16.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 11.05pt 0.5pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                 </span>Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 4.55pt 0.25pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                </span> [VIII of 2000] (Amended in 2003). </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.55pt .25pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 11 (Ka)</span></strong></p><p class="Style4" style="margin: 11.05pt 0.7pt 0.0001pt 0in; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The murder having taken place while the condemned-prisoner was living with his wife in the same house, he was under an obligation to explain how his wife had met with her death. In the absence of any explanation coming from his side, it seems that none other than the accused husband was responsible for causing the death in question. <span class="FontStyle18"><span style="mso-ansi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; font-weight: normal;">The State -Vs- Md. Mamun @ Mamun-Or-Rashid 5 ALR (HCD)2015(l) 107</span></span></span></p><p class="Style15" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span class="FontStyle29"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                  </span><strong><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Nari-0-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></span></span></p><p class="Style12" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span class="FontStyle20" style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal;">                                                      [VIII of 2000]</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.55pt .25pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span class="FontStyle29" style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Sections ll(kha) and 30</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 4.55pt .25pt .0001pt 0in;"><span class="FontStyle17"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; font-weight: normal;">The learned Judge of the Tribunal without any specific observation rejected the narajee petition which is not passed in accordance with law. Therefore, High Court held that the impugned order suffers from legal infirmities and directed to make further enquiry into the allegations made in the naraji petition filed by the informant by the competent authority in accordance with law.</span></span><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Md. Phul Miah, -Vs.-l. Abdul AH and 8 others 4 ALR 2014(2) 139</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0.15in 0.5pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">             </span>Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 2.65pt 0.5pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">       </span>[VIII of 2000]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.65pt .5pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section ll(kha)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The accused appellant did not use any deadly weapons for commission of injury and it also further appears that the victim was given treatment by local doctor and subsequently she was taken into hospital for her treatment. Thus it shows that the accused appellant at least do not have the mensrea to kill her. Considering the same and the extenuating circumstances the ends of justice will be met if the sentence is reduced to 10 years from life.<em>Abdul Aziz alias Azit - Vs.-The State. 4 ALR 2014(2)34.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 4.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections ll(kha) and 30 - Ingredients necessary for framing charges.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 1.9pt 1.45pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                                 </span>Penal Code </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>[XLV of 1860]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 313 and 315</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 2.15pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">All that is necessary at the stage of framing of the charge is to see whether a prima facie case has been made out regarding the commission of certain offences or offence. The truth and effect of the evidence to be adduced at the trial cannot be judged at this stage. In the present case, the accused stands charged for the offence punishable under section ll(kha), 30 of the Ain, 2000, and cognizance has been taken thereunder. Since a prima facie case has clearly been made out to go for the trial, there is nothing wrong in framing the impugned charges.<em>Ms.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Morzina Khatun- Vs.- Saiful Islam Sarkar 3 ALR(2014)(1) 335.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.05pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                         </span>Nari-0-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 5.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                                     </span>[VIII of 2000]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section ll(Kha) - Conviction even without framing charge on a particular count.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The accused may be convicted of the offence which was proved against him although no charge was framed.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Ingredients of section 11(a) of the Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Ain, 2000 are very much present in this case against the appellant-petitioner and in view of the provision of section 237 of the Code of Criminal Procedure he may be convicted of the offence which was proved against him although no charge was framed under section 11 (a) as the same offences are of cognate nature. Conviction of the appellant-petitioner under section 11(a) was rightly found to be in accordance with law.<em> Md. Harun-ur-Rashid -Vs.-TheState 3ALR(2014)(1)(AD) 104.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: .25pt 2.15pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                          </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                </span>Nari-0-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.4pt 1.7pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                             </span>[VIII of 2000](amended in 2003)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections ll(Ga) and 30 — Ad-interim bail by the High Court Division, Session Judge can not review the merit of the order of bail except misuse of the bail.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When High Court Division assessed the merit of the case in granting bail, the Sessions Judge is not competent to re­assess the merit of the case . He can, of course, examine the question of misuse of the privilege of the bail by the accused. <em>Hossain Md. Rajib vs State 4 ALR 2014(2) 70.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 11.05pt 1.45pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                        </span>Nari-0-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.65pt .95pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">     </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                                  </span>[VIII of 2000]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.9pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 11 (Ga)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The High Court Division found that the incident of assault on the complainant is alleged to have occurred on 06.02.2009, whereas the accused husband claims to have divorced the complainant on 19.01.2009. The High Court Division observed that since the divorce took place earlier, the victim was not supposed to be present in the house of her husband after 19.01.2009.<em>The State -Vs.- Md. Rofizal Haque, 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)90.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.9pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 17</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 9.85pt .95pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Appellate Division helds that before proceeding with a case of false complaint or information against the informant or complainant, it would be prudent for the Court or Tribunal concerned to examine the materials on record to assess the prima facie nature of the allegation. It would be a futile exercise to proceed against the complainant/informant of a case charging him with having lodged a false case if the allegation of a false case having been brought by the accused is ultimately not likely to be substantiated in Court. <em>A.K. Azad -Vs.- Md. Mostafizur Rahman 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)44.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 17 - On the basis of the narajee petition tribunal should be ordered to make further enquiry.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; tab-stops: 222.7pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The impugned order dated 07-02-2004 passed by learned Judge of Tribunal in Nari-O-Shishu Case no. 294 of 2003 is set aside. The learned Judge of the Tribunal is directed to make further enquiry into the allegations made in the narajee petition filed by the informant by the competent authority.<em> Masirunnecha - Vs.- Antad Sheikh. 4 ALR 2014(2) 253.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section-17(2)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sub-section (2) of section 17 of the Nari-O-Sishu Nirjatan Dmana Ain, 2000 authorises the Tribunal to take cognizance against of the offence of making a false complaint before it only on a written complaint by the aggrieved party and in such case procedures laid down in sections 200-203 are required to be complied with.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">In the absence of a written complaint before the Tribunal it has no power to allow the investigating officer to initiate a legal proceeding against the informant for making false allegations against the accused. <em>Harabilash Mitra -Vs.- Sanjoy Biswas 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 154.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 19(2), (3) and (4) - The Tribunal is empowered to exercise its jurisdiction as the Court of original jurisdiction until the case is ready for trial and then as the Trial Court.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Officer-in-Charge of a Police Station any other Police Officer making the arrest of an accused, the Investigating Officer or any other Officer empowered to investigate into the offences under the Ain is required by the Ain to forward the person arrested without any warrant or in execution of any warrant, or to send the information relating to the commission or suspicion of the commission of any offence under the Ain or to submit the investigation report, whatever it may be, through the G. R. O. directly to the concerned Tribunal and not to any other Court. Since, the Tribunal has been bestowed upon the jurisdiction of the Court of original jurisdiction under the Ain, it is also empowered to deal with bail even before the case is ready for trial inasmuch as Section 19(2), (3) and (4) exclusively empower the Tribunal to deal with the bail under the Ain, which does not differentiate the bail as to the bail during the investigation into or the bail during the trial of the case.<em>Md. Shahjahan and others - Vs. - The State. 4 ALR 2014(2) 167.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 21- Trial in absentia.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Under a special law, its trial and its all procedures should be continuing and concluded under the provisions of the special law. Following the requirements of section 21 of the Ain, 2000 is sufficient for trial in absentia. <em>Md. Mohor Ali -Vs.- The State 3 ALR(2014)(1) 347.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 22</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .25pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                        </span>Guardians and Wards Act, 1890</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 25 read with Majority Act, 1875</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.7pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The father is the well-wisher of his children and according to the Majority Act, 1875 one becomes major on attaining the age of 18 years. According to law father is the legal guardian of his children below 18 years of age and he is legally entitled to his/her custody. Whether the victim is a minor or major has to be determined by the Majority Act, 1875 and the question of custody must be determined in the light of the Majority Act, 1875 read with Guardians and Wards Act, 1890 coupled with the question of her wellbeing. <em>Sanjit Baidya - Vs.- The State 6 ALR -2015(2)211</em></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-0-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 69.1pt; text-align: center; text-indent: 80.15pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">[VIII of 2000] Section 27 (1- ka) read with</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.55pt; text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Code of Criminal Procedure </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">(V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .05in; text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 200 and 173 - The tribunal has discretion to assume cognisance even though the report was in the negaive.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 27(1 Ga) confers wide discretion upon the tribunal in that it can assume cognisance even if the Police Report, as contemplated by Section 173 Cr.P.C,exonerates the accused. This discretionary power is surely meant to prevent abuse or bias by investigators, which are not uncommon. As the records reveal, the police in the case in hand transmitted a negative report i.e a Final Report, and hence, under Section 27 (1ga) read with section 27(1), the tribunal had discretion to assume cognisance eventhough the report was in the negative. <em>Md. Mokbul Hossain Molla -Vs.-The State 6 ALR - 2015(2)196</em></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 11.05pt 4.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-0-Shishu Nirjatan Damon Ain</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 8.4pt 3.35pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">[VIII of 2000]</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 27 (1 Ka)(Ka)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .1in; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The intention of the legislature as reflected in section 27 (1 Ka)(Ka) is to empower the tribunal to direct "any Magistrate" or "any person" excluding any police officer to enquire and report within 7 working days. The expression "any person" in section 27 (lKa)(Ka), according to our view, does not include any "police officer" but it includes any public officer or any private individual or any other responsible person of the society upon whom the tribunal may have confidence to get the enquiry conducted in respect of the complaint lodged before the tribunal and submit report within seven working days. <em>Sirajul Islam @ A Suban-Vs.- The State and others 1 ALR(2012) (HCD) 162.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 27 (1) (Ga)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.25pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Before framing charge the petitioner came before the High Court by filing an application under section 561A Cr.P.C for quashing the order of cognizance passed by the Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Tribunal. The High Court Division held that the petitioner has scape and opportunity to agistate the matter by filing application u/s 265C of the Cr.P.C before the tribunal and as such the application U/s 561A Cr.P.C is not maintainable. <em>Nepal @ Nepal Chandra Saha - Vs. -The State 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 79.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 27,27(lka) and (I kha)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Jurisdiction of the Tribunal and its power to take cognizance</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.65pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">27(1)-The Tribunal shall not take cognizance of an offence except without jatan Daman Ain a report by a Police officer not below the rank of sub -Inspector.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 5.75pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section (lka)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">On failure of the complainant to record an FIR at the Police Station, although urged, he may file a complaint to the the Tribunal, duly attended by an affidavit in support of his authority. In such a case the Tribunal after examing the complainant, if satisfied, may send the complaint to any allegation or any other person to enquire into the matter and to report within 7 working days. On consideration of the enquiry report and the complaint if the Tribunal is satisfied about the existence of aprima faciecase, he will take cognizance and proceed with the trial. <em>Babu Miah-Vs.- The State 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 338.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 1.2pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 27 (lkha) </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">—If on receipt of the enquiry report the Tribunal does not find a prima facie case for trial, he shall dismiss the complaint as unsubstantiated. <em>Babu Miah-Vs.- The State (Criminal) 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 338.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 27 (IGa)—</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The Tribunal has no power to take cognizance just on the basis of a naraji petition. <em>Babu Miah-Vs.- The State 2 ALR (2013)(HCD) 338.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 28- </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">No requirement in law for recording the reasons for framing charge elaborately. - There is no direction either in section 265C or in any other section of the Code of Criminal Procedure that the court/tribunal will have to record the reasons of framing charge also. If the Court/Tribunal, on examination of the records and also after hearing both the sides finds that there are sufficient materials for proceeding against the accused the Court/Tribunal shall frame charge against the accused persons, there is no requirement in law for recording the reasons for framing charge elaborately. <em>Md. Muntasir Mamun Khan -Vs.- The State (Criminal) 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 77.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 5.5pt 1.45pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.65pt 1.7pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 28 </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- Whether enlarged the convict on bail after he had suffered only seven months out of his sentence of 14 years imprisonment - The Appellate Division held that from the impugned order it appears that while granting bail the High Court Division considered the evidence and materials on record as well as the facts and circumstances of the case and exercised its discretion to grant bail to the respondent. The Appellate Division also considered the evidence and materials on record. In the facts and circumstances of the case the Appellate Division consider that the exercise of discretion calls for any interference by this Division. <em>The State-Vs.-S.M. Mizanur Rahman 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 50.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 2.65pt 1.7pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 9.35pt 0in .0001pt 13.45pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman (Bishes Bidhan) Ain</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 9.35pt 0in .0001pt 13.45pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">[XVIII of 1995]</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 6(1) - Sexual intercourse with consent is not a rape.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">There was a continuous consent of the complainant for sexual intercourse with the accused which will not come within the purview of rape as laid down in Ain, 1995, therefore, the learned Judge without complying the Provisions of law most erroneously framed charge under Section 6(1) of the Ain, 1995.<em>Idris Miah -Vs.-<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Arafa Begum 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 70.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 10(1) - Husband's is to explain when the wife was in his custody and met with her dead.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When the wife met with her death while she was in the custody of her husband it is he who is to explain how she met with her death. It rather appears from the evidence that he allowed his wife to die and even after her death he did not inform any of the co-villagers or reported the matter to the police. None of the inmates of the house belonging to the convict also informed the police nor took any proper medical help for saving the life of the victim. The murder having taken place while the condemned convict was living with his wife in the same house he was under an obligation to explain how his wife had met with her death. In the absence of any explanation coming from his side it seems none other than the husband who was responsible for causing the death in question. <em>The State -Vs.- Asah Uddin 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 35.</em></span></p><p> </p></div></div>

<w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="72" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful List Accent 2"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="73" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Grid Accent 2"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="60" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Shading Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="61" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light List Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="62" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Grid Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="63" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Shading 1 Accent 3"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="64"
