<w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="39" QFormat="true" Name="TOC Heading"/> </w:LatentStyles></xml><![endif]--><!-- [if gte mso 10]><style> /* Style Definitions */ table.MsoNormalTable	{mso-style-name:"Table Normal";	mso-tstyle-rowband-size:0;	mso-tstyle-colband-size:0;	mso-style-noshow:yes;	mso-style-priority:99;	mso-style-qformat:yes;	mso-style-parent:"";	mso-padding-alt:0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;	mso-para-margin-top:0in;	mso-para-margin-right:0in;	mso-para-margin-bottom:10.0pt;	mso-para-margin-left:0in;	line-height:115%;	mso-pagination:widow-orphan;	font-size:11.0pt;	mso-bidi-font-size:14.0pt;	font-family:"Angsana New","serif";	mso-hansi-font-family:Calibri;	mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;	mso-bidi-language:BN;}</style><![endif]--></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 11.3pt 2.4pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">                      Negotiable Instruments Act</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 5.05pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">                   [XXVI of 1881]</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; mso-pagination: widow-orphan; margin: 3.35pt 5.05pt .0001pt 0in;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .25pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 7 and 138(1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .25pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The cheque drawn by the accused petitioner on the bank account is not maintained in her name rather it is maintained in the name of her husband. For the purpose of Section 138(1) of the Act, the account has to be maintained by the drawer of the cheque. The liability or debt of the husband cannot be thrust on to the shoulder of the wife, the accused-petitioner. The impugned proceeding is quashed. <em>Shahnaj Begum Munni. -Vs-The State 1 ALR (HCD) 56.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 13 and 138</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: 4.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 13 of the Negotiable Instrument Act 1881 which has defined "Negotiable Instrument" has not made any distinction between "crossed cheque account payee" or "post-dated cheque given as a security for repayment of the loan" or " any other cheque issued by the drawer for encashment currently" or cheque of other kinds such as "bearer cheque" as ordinarily mean. <em>Tipu Sultan - Vs. - The State 6 ALR</em> <em>2015(2)190.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 123 A</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .25pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">All cheques whether "crossed cheque account payee" or cheque of other kind such as "bearer cheque" are all "Negotiable Instrument" and section 123 A of the N.I. Act does not create any bar in proceeding with a case under section 138 of the Act, 1881 and the moment a cheque is dishonored, either a bearer cheque or crossed cheque "account payee", for any reason specified in section 138, the offence under the section shall be completed and in that case the payee shall have the liberty to file a petition of complaint before the competent Magistrate against the drawer of the cheque by complying with the proviso to sub-section (1) of section 138.<em>Tipu Sultan - Vs. - The State 6 ALR</em> <em>2015(2)190.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 123A and 138 - Crossed cheque.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The legislative mandate as used in clause (a) of sub-section (2) of section 123 A of the Act, 1881 that when a cheque is crossed "account payee" shall cease to be negotiable means it cannot be negotiated or encashed with any other person except the person in whose favour the same was issued. To make it clearer, a crossed cheque "account payee" must be enchased through the account of the holder in whose favour it was issued. So, by no means, a crossed cheque "account payee" loses its character as a negotiable one within the meaning of section 138 of the Act, 1881. Moreover, section 13 of Act, 1881 which has defined "Negotiable instrument" has not made any distinction between crossed cheque "account payee" or cheque of other kind such as bearer cheque we ordinarily mean. Thus, we find that section 123 A of the Act, in no way, creates any bar in proceeding with a case under section 138 of the Act, 1881. In other words, we do not see any nexus of section 123A with the proceedings to be initiated under section 138 of the Act. <em>Md. Sahab Uddin - Vs.- The State 3 ALR(2014)(1)(AD) 111.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138 <span style="letter-spacing: .5pt;">read with</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                                  </span>Code of Criminal Procedure</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif'; letter-spacing: .5pt;">[V of 1898]</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 439A, 439 (1), 423, 426,427 and 428</span></strong></p><p class="Style4" style="line-height: normal; margin: 7.7pt 2.15pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Keeping in mind the sentencing principles let the Appellate Division consider whether the High Court Division is justified in enhancing the sentences of fine suo moto in the absence of filing revision petitions by the complainant. The petitioner was convicted in the cases pursuant to complaints made by the complainant. Section 417A empowers the complainant to prefer appeal to the appellate court against the sentence on the ground of its in adequacy. Sub­section (3) of Section 417A provides that when an appeal has been filed against sentence on the ground of its inadequacy, the appellate court shall not enhance the sentence except after giving to the accused reasonable opportunity of showing cause against such enhancement. The similar principle will be applicable in cases of inadequacy or reduction of sentence passed by the appellate Court in view of section 439(1) of the Code of Criminal Procedure (the Code) under which provision, the revisional court has been given all the powers conferred on a court of appeal by sections 423, 426, 427 and 428 of the Code. <em>Shahidur Rahman Khadem-Vs-The State and others 6 ALR (AD) 2015 (2)218.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .15in; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The High Court Division considered that in demanding the payment of money by issuing a notice under clause (b) of the proviso to section 138 of the N.l. Act, the payee or the holder in due course of the cheque must demand for the payment of the amount covered by the cheque nor any higher or lesser amount of the cheque and if the demand is made for a lesser amount or for a big amount not covered by the cheque, which was dishonored the prosecution case must fail as the statutory requirements of section 138 of the N.I. Act has not been fulfilled. <em>Md. Belal Uddin -Vs.- Alhaj Md. Lutfor Rahman 6 ALR - 2015(2)38.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .15in; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.55pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138 of the Negotiable instruments Act, Is not an isolated enactment and since the same does not contain non obstante clause as such the same is to be provisions of the said Act.Thus when the trial commences the said law entitle the accused person to take any defence. In the light of section 4,6,8,9,43,58 and 118 of the said Act, <em>Uttam Kumar Sarkar and others -Vs.- The State 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 82</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138 </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- An offence under section 138 of the Negotiable Instruments Act is not compoundable, it being a special law. The ends of Justice will be sufficiently met if the sentence of the petitioner is reduced to imprisonment for the period already undergone by him in prison, and the sentence of fine is set aside. <em>Md. Idris Chowkder - Vs.- The State 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 83.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138 </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- Section 138(1) empowers the trial Court to punish with imprisonment for a maximum period of one year, or with fine which may extend to thrice the amount of the cheque or both. The powers given to the Court is discretionary. The language used in the section is not such that the Court must impose fine thrice the amount of the cheque. The legislature has left the matter to the discretion of the trial Court. <em>Shahidur Rahman Khadem -Vs.-The State 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 14.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138 </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">- The allegations of bouncing of cheque simpliciter does not ipso facto constitute any offence as defined under section 115 dt of the Penal Code punishable under section 420 of the Penal Code and as such, framing of charge against the appellant under section 420 of the Penal Code suffered from serious illegality. <em>M. A. Sukkur -Vs.- Md. Zahirul Haque and another 5 ALR (AD)2015(1) 27.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .7pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 8.15pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">As section 138 of the Negotiable Instrument Act is a special law the time limit has been framed by the legislature which are required to be followed strictly before institution of the case thus a notice for demanding money is required to give absolutely on or before within 15 days of the receipt of information.<em>Murari Mohan Datta @ Sree Mohan Datta-Vs.-Bhabal Roy Chowdhury and another. 4 ALR 2014(2) 151</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 138 and 141(b)- Criminal proceeding should not be stifled before trial, when there is a prima facie case for going to the trial.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">There was no violation of section 141(b) of the Negotiable Instrument Act. The High Court Division further found that the law is now settled on the point that a criminal proceeding should not be stifled before trial, when there is a prima facie case for going to the trial.<em>M.K. Bazlur Rahman -Vs.- Md. Johurul Haque 3 ALR(2014)(1)(AD) 107.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section-138 Punishment for dishonour of cheque due to insufficiency of fund etc.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.35pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Dishonour of cheque by the bank due to fraudulent action of the drawer clearly brings him within the mischief of the offence u/s 138 of the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881. 'Stopping of payment' by the drawer with oblique motive also brings him within the mischief of section 138 of the Act, although the drawer has the right to stop payment on genuine grounds.<em>S.M. Redwan -Vs.- Md. Rezaul Islam and others 3ALR(2014)(1)(AD)62.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.3pt; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138 C(l)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Even through the petition of complaint was filed before the expiry of 30 days from the date of receipt of the notice as laid down in proviso (c) of sub-Section (1) of the section 138 of the Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881, but the pre­maturity of the proceeding cured before taking cognizance by the Court of Sessions. <em>Fazle Rabbi Md. Enamul Huq -Vs.-Md. Ali Hasan Baktar and another. 4 ALR 2014(2) 181.</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 10.1pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138 (l)(b) - The bouncing of a cheque a notice is served under proviso (b) of section 138(1), the proceeding must be initiated within one month from the date of failure of the drawer.</span></strong></p><p class="Style7" style="line-height: normal; margin: 7.7pt 0.25pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">The settled position of law is that the payee or holder of a cheque in due course can present a cheque as many times as he or she wishes within the period of validity of the cheque and at his or her option can choose on which bouncing of the cheque shall initiate a proceeding under section 138 of the Act. The only limitation is that once on the bouncing of a cheque a notice is served under proviso ALR Criminal* Forma-14 (b) of section 138(1), the proceeding must be initiated within one month from the date of failure on the part of the drawer to pay the amount within 30 days of the receipt of notice. If after service of notice the drawer fails to pay the amount within 30 days and the payee does not initiate a proceeding within one month there from as provided in section 141, the payee forfeits his right to initiate a proceeding under section 138 of the Act.<em>Md. Abu Bakar -Vs.- The State and another 5 ALR (HCD)2015(1) 73.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 11.5pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Section 138 — Punishment for dishonour of a cheque if payment is not made within 15 days after receipt of a legal notice intimating dishonor of the cheque.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 7.45pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">It has been consistently held by the Appellate Division that there is nothing in law that precludes a criminal case on account of the pending of a civil suit on the same fact. The criminal case stands for the offence u/s 138 of the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881 while the civil suit is for realization of mony and as such both cases proceed independently. <em>Ehetasamul Hague vs5The State 3 ALR(2014)(1) 243</em></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';"> <br/></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.85pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">Sections 138 and 140 - Company is no necessary party Director represents the company.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 9.6pt; text-align: justify; text-justify: inter-ideograph; mso-pagination: widow-orphan;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman','serif';">When the Managing Director of the Company is made party, there is no necessity for making the Company a party as he represents the company. <em>Mr. Younusuzzaman (Badal) -Vs.-The State 3 ALR(2014)(1) 438.</em></span></p></div></div>
